Beginning of the Wiping Period and Gender Equality
Ruling statement on timing and equality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact moment when the permissible period for wiping over khuffs begins, calculate its duration for a resident and a traveler, and confirm that the ruling applies equally to men and women.

Core Idea
The clock for wiping over khuffs starts after the first hadath, not when you put them on.

This short passage from the Jawharah al-Nayirah clarifies a key timing rule for the concession of wiping over khuffs. A common mistake is to think the count begins at the moment of wearing the khuffs, but the Hanafi school explicitly ties it to the first hadath. Additionally, the ruling is identical for both genders, emphasizing the general applicability of this dispensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is wiping over khuffs (al-mash ala al-khuffayn), a permissible substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
The passage does not restate the basic permissibility but specifies the timing.
2
Determine the starting point of the period
The text says 'ابتداؤها عقيب الحدث' — the beginning is immediately after the hadath (ritual impurity). This means the count starts from the moment you break your wudu after having worn the khuffs in a state of purity.
Not from the time of wearing or from the first prayer.
3
Calculate the duration for a resident
For a resident, the permissible period is 'يوماً وليلة' — one day and one night, i.e., 24 hours from the moment of the hadath.
The phrase 'من وقت الحدث إلى مثله' confirms counting from the time of hadath to the same time the next day.
4
Calculate the duration for a traveler
For a traveler, the period extends to three days and three nights — 'في الثلاث للمسافر' meaning three full days and nights from the hadath.
The traveler's longer period is a concession for the hardship of travel.
5
Recognize gender equality
The final sentence 'والرجل والمرأة فيه سواء' explicitly states that the rule applies equally to men and women. No distinction in timing or conditions based on gender.
This is straightforward and needs no further qualification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابتداؤها عقيب الحدث. يعني من وقت الحدث إلى مثله، للمقيم : يوماً وليلة، وإلى مثله في الثلاث للمسافر. والرجل والمرأة فيه سواء.
Its beginning is immediately after the hadath. Meaning: from the time of the hadath to the same time, for the resident: a day and a night, and to the same time in the three for the traveler. And the man and the woman are equal in it.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage explains the start of the permissible wiping period. The phrase 'beginning is immediately after the hadath' means that once a valid hadath occurs after wearing khuffs in a state of complete purity, the clock starts. For a resident, the wipe validity lasts exactly one day and night from that moment; for a traveler, three days and nights. The commentator emphasizes that the count is from the moment of the first hadath to the corresponding time on the last day. There is no distinction between men and women—the same rules apply to both.

Key Terms
ابتداؤها (ibtidā'uhā): The beginning of the period during which wiping is permissible after the hadath.
عقيب الحدث (uqayb al-ḥadath): Immediately following the occurrence of a ritual impurity (hadath).
المقيم (al-muqīm): The resident, not on a journey.
المسافر (al-musāfir): The traveler, considered on a journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the permissible duration for wiping over khuffs begin?
A) At the time of wearing the khuffs
B) At the moment of the first hadath after wearing them in purity
C) At the time of the first prayer after wearing
D) At dawn

Key Takeaway
The permissible wiping period begins at the moment of the first hadath after wearing khuffs in purity, and it applies equally to men and women.

The Sunnah and Fard Methods of Wiping over Khuffs
Distinguishes sunnah and fard methods of wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the sunnah and fard methods of wiping over khuffs and apply the three-finger minimum rule to determine validity.

Core Idea
The fard in wiping khuffs is only three fingers' width; the detailed finger-stroke method is sunnah, not required.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira clarifies two layers of the wiping act: the recommended (sunnah) method taught by the Prophet ﷺ and the minimal required amount (fard) that makes the wipe valid. Understanding the distinction prevents unnecessary hardship while preserving the sunnah's merit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components of wiping
Read the text and note that wiping over khuffs has a sunnah method (المسنون) and a fard minimum (المفروض). They are distinct obligations: one is recommended, the other necessary for validity.
The sunnah method is more detailed but not obligatory; the fard is the bare minimum.
2
Describe the sunnah method
Extract from the text: wipe the upper surface with the fingers of each hand, placing them on the front of the respective khuff and drawing them in lines (خطوطاً) upward to above the ankle, with fingers spread. Repetition is not required because it erases the lines.
The word 'خطوطاً' indicates a single stroke per finger.
3
State the fard minimum
The obligatory amount is the area of three fingers (مقدار ثلاث أصابع) on the upper surface. This can be achieved by any means: wiping with fingers, plunging feet into water, rain splashes, or even a stick.
The three fingers are approximate width; exact finger size is not critical.
4
Analyze permissible alternatives
The text lists methods to fulfill the fard: wiping with palm, immersion, rain, or a stick. All are valid as long as three fingers' area gets wet. Also, wiping from the leg down to the toes (opposite direction) is acceptable.
Direction does not affect validity; only the wetted area matters.
5
Identify the Hanafi vs. other school difference
Other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki) require wiping the entire upper surface. The Hanafi view allows a minimal area, making it easier in cold or difficult conditions.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمسح على الخفين على ظاهرهما خطوطاً بالأصابع. هذا هو المسنون، ولو مسح براحته: جاز. وقوله : خطوطاً : إشارة إلى أنه لا يُشترط التكرار؛ لأن بالتكرار تنعدم الخطوط. وصورة المسح : أن يضع أصابع يده اليمنى على مُقدَّم خفه الأيمن، وأصابع يده اليسرى على مُقدَّم خُفّه الأيسر، ويمدهما جميعاً إلى الساق فوق الكعبين، ويُفرِّجَ بين أصابعه، هذا هو المسنون. وأما المفروض فمقدار ثلاث أصابع سواء مَسَحَ بالأصابع، أو خاض في الماء، أو أصاب خفيه ماء المطر مقدار ثلاث أصابع. وكذا لو مسح بعود. أو من قبل الساق إلى الأصابع.
And wiping over the khuffs is on their upper surfaces with lines with the fingers. This is the sunnah, and if he wipes with his palm, it is permissible. And his statement: 'with lines' indicates that repetition is not required, because with repetition the lines vanish. The form of sunnah wiping: he places the fingers of his right hand on the front of his right khuff, and the fingers of his left hand on the front of his left khuff, and draws them both to the leg above the ankles, and he spreads his fingers. This is the sunnah. As for the fard (obligatory minimum), it is the amount of three fingers, whether he wipes with his fingers, or plunges his feet into water, or rain water hits his khuffs to the extent of three fingers. Similarly, if he wipes with a stick. Or from the leg to the toes.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage details the method of wiping. It distinguishes between the recommended (sunnah) method and the minimal requirement (fard). The sunnah method: wiping the upper surface of each khuff with the fingers of the respective hand in straight lines from the toes upward to above the ankle, with the fingers spread apart. Repeating strokes is not required; a single line per finger suffices. Wiping with the palm is permissible but not sunnah. The fard—which validates the wipe—is to cover an area equivalent to three fingers (roughly the width of three digits) on any part of the upper surface. This can be done by any means: wiping with fingers, immersing the foot in water, walking through puddles, or even a stick, as long as three fingers' area is wetted. The direction from leg to toes is also mentioned as acceptable.

Key Terms
المسنون (al-masnūn): The recommended method of wiping: with fingers, in lines, from front to above ankle.
المفروض (al-mafrūḍ): The obligatory minimum: an area equivalent to three fingers on the upper surface.
خطوطاً (khuṭūṭan): Lines: indicating a single stroke per finger without repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum area that must be wiped for the wiping to be valid (fard)?
A) The entire upper surface
B) One finger's width
C) Three fingers' width
D) The entire khuff including the sole

Key Takeaway
The fard for wiping khuffs is only three fingers' area; the sunnah method is a separate, recommended practice.

The Obligatory Minimum and Method of Wiping over Khuffain
Expands on rulings for wiping over khuffain: duration, sunnah and fard methods, conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fard amount and recommended method for wiping over khuffain, and identify conditions that invalidate the wiping.

Core Idea
The obligatory minimum for wiping is three fingers from the hand; the sunnah is lines with fingers from toes to leg.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings on wiping over khuffain, distinguishing between the sunnah method and the fard minimum. You will learn the precise obligatory amount, the recommended technique, and the critical condition that the khuff must be free of large tears. The passage also clarifies the duration of wiping for residents and travelers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the duration of wiping
Determine the period for which wiping is valid after hadath: for a resident, one day and one night; for a traveler, three days and nights. The clock starts immediately after the hadath.
Men and women are equal in this ruling.
2
Distinguish sunnah from fard method
The sunnah method is to wipe the outer surface of each khuff in lines with spread fingers from the toes up to the leg above the ankle, without repetition. The fard (obligatory) is any wiping that covers an area equivalent to three fingers from the hand.
Wiping with the palm or by stepping in water suffices if three fingers' area is covered.
3
Identify invalidating conditions
Wiping is invalid if the khuff has a large tear, or if the wiping is done on the inner surface, from the heel, or with less than three fingers (e.g., one or two fingers).
Wiping width-wise or with three fingers placed but not extended is valid but not sunnah.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Karkhi held that the measure is three fingers from the foot, but the majority (including the commentator) view that it is from the hand because the hand is the instrument of wiping. The latter is the relied-upon position.
Tarjih: 'The first is more correct' (al-awwal asahh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين
ابتداؤها عقيب الحدث.
والمسح على الخفين على ظاهرهما خطوطاً بالأصابع،
وليلة، والمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها (١).
* قوله : (ابتداؤها : عَقِيب الحدث : يعني من وقت الحدث إلى مثله، للمقيم : يوماً وليلة، وإلى مثله في الثلاث للمسافر.
والرجل والمرأة فيه سواء.
قوله: (والمسح على الخفين على ظاهرهما خطوطاً بالأصابع).
هذا
هو المسنون، ولو مسح براحته: جاز.
وقوله : خطوطاً : إشارة إلى أنه لا يُشترط التكرار؛ لأن بالتكرار
تنعدم الخطوط.
وصورة المسح : أن يضع أصابع يده اليمنى على مُقدَّم خفه الأيمن، وأصابع يده اليسرى على مُقدَّم خُفّه الأيسر، ويمدهما جميعاً إلى الساق فوق الكعبين، ويُفرِّجَ بين أصابعه، هذا هو المسنون.
وأما المفروض فمقدار ثلاث أصابع سواء مَسَحَ بالأصابع، أو خاض في الماء، أو أصاب خفيه ماء المطر مقدار ثلاث أصابع.

يجزئه.

ولا يجوز المسح على خُفٌ فيه خُرْقٌ كبيرٌ
أو مسح عليهما عرضاً: أجزأه، إلا أنه غير مسنون. وكذا إذا مسح بثلاث أصابع موضوعة غير ممدودة: يجزئه. ولو مشى على الحشيش المبتل بالماء أو بالمطر: أجزاء.
ولو مسح بأصبع واحدة، أو بأصبعين: لا يجزئه.
والمستحب أن يمسح بباطن الكف، ولو مسح بظاهر كفيه: أجزأه. ولو مسح على باطن خفيه أو من قبل العقب، أو من جوانبهما : لا

هذا هو المسنون، ويكفيه المسح مرة واحدة. ولو بدأ من الساق إلى الأصابع : جاز.

وقال الكرخي من أصابع الرجل.
والأول أصح؛ اعتباراً لآلة المسح؛ لأن المسح بها يقع.
* قوله : (ولا يجوز المسح على خُفٌ فيه خُرْق كبير).
Chapter of wiping over the khuffain. Its beginning is immediately after the hadath (minor impurity). And wiping over the khuffain is on their outer surface in lines with the fingers. (For the resident) one day and one night, and for the traveler three days and their nights (1). * His saying: (Its beginning is immediately after the hadath) meaning from the time of hadath to its like, for the resident one day and one night, and to its like in the three for the traveler. The man and woman are equal in this. His saying: (And wiping over the khuffain on their outer surface in lines with the fingers). This is the sunnah, and if he wiped with his palm, it is permissible. And his saying: 'in lines' indicates that repetition is not required because with repetition the lines would disappear. And the description of the wiping: he places the fingers of his right hand on the front of his right khuff, and the fingers of his left hand on the front of his left khuff, and extends both together to the leg above the ankles, and spreads his fingers. This is the sunnah. As for the obligatory (mafrud), it is the amount of three fingers, whether he wiped with fingers, or waded in water, or rain water hit his khuff to the extent of three fingers. Similarly, if he wiped with a stick. Or from the leg to the toes. (1) Sahih Muslim (276). He begins from the tips of the toes to the leg. It suffices him. And the obligatory of that is the amount of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand. And it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff that has a large tear. Or if he wiped width-wise, it suffices him, except it is not sunnah. Similarly, if he wiped with three fingers placed not extended, it suffices him. And if he walked on wet grass or rain, it suffices. And if he wiped with one finger or two, it does not suffice him. And it is recommended to wipe with the inner palm, and if he wiped with the outer part of his palms, it suffices him. And if he wiped on the inner part of his khuff or from the heel or from their sides, it does not (suffice). * His saying: (He begins from the tips of the fingers to the leg). This is the sunnah, and one wiping suffices him. And if he began from the leg to the fingers, it is permissible. * His saying: (And the obligatory of that is the amount of three fingers from the fingers of the hand). Al-Karkhi said: from the fingers of the foot. The first is more correct, considering the instrument of wiping because wiping occurs with it. * His saying: (And it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff that has a large tear).
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This is an expansion probe from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah commenting on Al-Mukhtasar by Al-Quduri. It opens the chapter on wiping over khuffain (leather socks) in wudu. The passage addresses three main areas: (1) the time period of wiping, (2) the method and obligatory amount, and (3) conditions of the khuff. The period begins right after breaking wudu (hadath) and lasts for a resident one day and one night, and for a traveler three days and nights, based on a hadith from Sahih Muslim. Men and women are equal. The sunnah method is to wipe the outer surface of each khuff starting from the toes up to the leg above the ankle, using the fingers spread out and drawing lines without repetition. However, the fard (obligatory) minimum is the amount of three fingers from the hand; any method achieving this suffices, such as wiping with the palm, stepping in water, or rain. Wiping with one or two fingers does not suffice. The khuff must not have a large tear; otherwise wiping is invalid. Al-Karkhi opined that the measure is from the foot's fingers, but the preferred view is from the hand because the hand is the instrument of wiping.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or footwear that covers the feet up to the ankles, worn for wiping in wudu.
مسح (mash): The act of wiping over the khuff with a wet hand as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
مفروض (mafrud): The obligatory minimum amount of wiping, which is the extent of three fingers from the hand.
حدث (hadath): Minor impurity that nullifies wudu, triggering the need for wudu and the permission to wipe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum obligatory amount for wiping over khuffain according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) The entire outer surface of the khuff
B) The amount of three fingers from the hand
C) The amount of three fingers from the foot
D) A single line with the index finger

Key Takeaway
The fard minimum for wiping over khuffain is three fingers from the hand; the sunnah method is detailed but not required, and a large tear invalidates the khuff.

Rulings on Wiping over Khuffs: Fard, Sunnah, and Holes
Explains fard amount, sunnah method, and effect of holes on wiping validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs, state the fard amount and sunnah method, and distinguish between valid and invalid holes using the Hanafi istihsan argument.

Core Idea
A large hole (exposing three foot fingers) invalidates wiping over khuffs; small holes are tolerated due to custom and hardship.

This lesson examines the detailed rulings for wiping over khuffs (leather socks) as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu. We will cover the obligatory (fard) area, the recommended (sunnah) method, and the critical condition regarding holes – a point of dispute between the Hanafi school and others. Understanding these distinctions ensures that your wudu is valid when wearing khuffs.

Guided Path
1
Identify fard and sunnah elements
Locate the obligatory amount (three smallest hand fingers) and the recommended method (starting from toes, using inner palm). Note the intra-Hanafi dispute with al-Karkhi.
The hand is the instrument of wiping, so its fingers are used to measure the fard area.
2
Define a large hole
A large hole is defined as exposing three of the smallest fingers of the foot. Holes in one khuff are combined to reach this measure; holes in two khuffs are not.
The measure differs from the fard measure: here it is foot fingers, not hand fingers.
3
Trace the Hanafi response to opposing schools
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that any hole invalidates wiping. The Hanafi response uses istihsan: khuffs customarily have small holes, so requiring removal causes hardship; large holes are rare, so no hardship.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
4
Apply the ruling to a case with multiple small holes
If a khuff has several small holes whose combined exposure equals three foot fingers, the wiping is invalid because they are combined. Practice applying the rules from the passage.
The author's example of combining holes is crucial for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين
يبدأ من رؤوس أصابع الرّجل إلى الساق. يجزئه. وفَرْضُ ذلك مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد . ولا يجوز المسح على خُفٌ فيه خُرْقٌ كبيرٌ أو مسح عليهما عرضاً: أجزأه، إلا أنه غير مسنون. وكذا إذا مسح بثلاث أصابع موضوعة غير ممدودة: يجزئه. ولو مشى على الحشيش المبتل بالماء أو بالمطر: أجزاء. ولو مسح بأصبع واحدة، أو بأصبعين: لا يجزئه. والمستحب أن يمسح بباطن الكف، ولو مسح بظاهر كفيه: أجزأه. ولو مسح على باطن خفيه أو من قبل العقب، أو من جوانبهما : لا
* قوله : (يبتدئ من رؤوس الأصابع إلى الساق). هذا هو المسنون، ويكفيه المسح مرة واحدة. ولو بدأ من الساق إلى الأصابع : جاز.
* قوله : (وفَرْضُ ذلك : مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصابع اليد). وقال الكرخي من أصابع الرجل. والأول أصح؛ اعتباراً لآلة المسح؛ لأن المسح بها يقع.
* قوله : (ولا يجوز المسح على خُفٌ فيه خُرْق كبير). يبين منه مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصابع الرّجل . يروى : بالباء الموحدة، وبالثاء المثلثة، فالأول: في موضع، والثاني: في مواضع. وفيه إشارة إلى أن الخروق تُجمع في خف واحد، ولا تُجمع في خفين بخلاف النجاسة المتفرقة ؛ لأنه حامل للكل. وانكشاف العورة: نظير النجاسة. وعند زفر، والشافعي): الخُرق اليسير يمنع المسح وإن قل؛ لأنه لما وجب غسل البادي: يجب غسل الباقي. قلنا : الخفافُ لا تخلو عن يسيرِ خُرق عادةً، فيلحقه الحرج في النزع، وتخلو عن الكبير : فلا حرج. والكبير : أن ينكشف منه مقدار ثلاث أصابع الرجل.
* قوله: (يَبينُ منه مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصابع الرجل): يعني أصغرها، هو الصحيح ؛ لأن الأصل في القدم هو الأصابع، باعتبار أنها أصل الرجل، والقدمُ تَبَع لها، ولهذا قالوا: إن مَن قَطَعَ أصابعَ رِجل إنسان فإنه يلزمه جميع الدية والثلاث أكثرها، فقامت مقام الكل، واعتبار الأصغر؛ للاحتياط. وفي المحيط» : إذا كان يبدو قَدْرُ ثلاث أنامل، وأسافلُها مستورة:
Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. He begins from the tips of the toes to the shank. It suffices him. And the fard of that is the measure of three fingers of the smallest fingers of the hand. And it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff that has a large hole. Or if he wiped over them crosswise: it suffices him, except that it is not sunnah. Similarly, if he wiped with three fingers placed but not stretched: it suffices. And if he walked on wet grass due to water or rain: it suffices. And if he wiped with one finger or two fingers: it does not suffice. And it is recommended to wipe with the inner palm; if he wiped with the back of his hands: it suffices. And if he wiped on the inner side of his khuffs or from the heel or from their sides: it does not. * His saying: (He begins from the tips of the toes to the shank). This is the sunnah, and one wipe suffices him. And if he began from the shank to the toes: it is permissible. * His saying: (And the fard of that is the measure of three fingers of the fingers of the hand). And al-Karkhi said: from the fingers of the foot. And the first is more correct, considering the instrument of wiping, because wiping occurs with it. * His saying: (And it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff that has a large hole). There appears from it the measure of three fingers of the fingers of the foot. It is narrated: with the single baa and with the triple thaa, the first in one place, the second in places. And in it is an indication that holes are combined in one khuff and are not combined in two khuffs, contrary to scattered impurity, because he carries the whole. And exposure of the private parts is analogous to impurity. And with Zufar and al-Shafi'i: a small hole prevents wiping even if small, because when washing the exposed part becomes obligatory, the rest must be washed. We said: Khuffs are not free from a small hole customarily, so hardship in removal would afflict him, and they are free from a large hole, so no hardship. And the large one: that from which the measure of three fingers of the foot is exposed. * His saying: (There appears from it the measure of three fingers of the fingers of the foot): meaning the smallest ones, that is the correct one, because the basis of the foot is the fingers, considering that they are the origin of the foot, and the foot is subordinate to them. This is why they said: Whoever cuts the fingers of a person's foot must pay the full diyah, and three are the majority, so they stand in place of the whole, and considering the smallest is for precaution. And in al-Muhit: if the measure of three finger-joints appears while their undersides are covered:
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses the rulings of wiping over khuffs (leather socks). It begins with the sunnah method: starting from the toes up to the shank, and one wipe suffices; starting from the shank is also permissible. The fard (obligatory) amount of wiping is the area covered by three of the smallest fingers of the hand. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Karkhi considered it to be three fingers of the foot, but the author states that the correct view is the hand fingers, because the hand is the instrument of wiping. The passage then discusses conditions for validity: wiping crosswise suffices but is not recommended; wiping with the inner palm is recommended; wiping with one or two fingers is insufficient. The main issue is holes in the khuff. The matn states that a large hole invalidates wiping. The sharh clarifies that 'large' means exposing three of the smallest fingers of the foot. Holes in one khuff are combined (to reach the threshold), but holes in two khuffs are not combined, unlike scattered impurity. The author presents an inter-madhhab dispute: Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that even a small hole prevents wiping, reasoning that if any part is exposed, it must be washed, and then the rest must follow. The Hanafi response relies on istihsan: khuffs customarily have small holes, so requiring removal would cause hardship; large holes are uncommon, so no hardship. The preferred position is that small holes do not prevent wiping. A specific citation from al-Muhit further discusses cases where only finger-joints are exposed.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock worn over the feet during wudu, allowing wiping instead of washing the feet.
خرق (kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff; the text distinguishes between small and large holes.
مسح (mash): The act of wiping the wet hand over the khuff as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
مقدار ثلاث أصابع (miqdar thalaath asaabi'): The measure of three fingers; used both for the obligatory wiped area (three hand fingers) and for the size of a large hole (three foot fingers).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what size hole in a khuff prevents valid wiping?
A) Any hole, even as small as a needle.
B) A hole that exposes three of the smallest fingers of the foot.
C) A hole that exposes three of the smallest fingers of the hand.
D) A hole that is covered by the foot when worn.

Key Takeaway
The validity of wiping over khuffs depends on the absence of a large hole (exposing three small foot fingers); small holes are tolerated due to customary hardship (istihsan).

Permissible Hole Size for Wiping over Khuffs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the size of hole excusing removal of khuff

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the permissible hole size for masah over khuffs and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani.

Core Idea
Holes exposing less than three small toes are excused; the preferred view requires three complete toes.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses a practical problem: what if the khuff has a hole? The Hanafi school balances strict qiyas with the ease of istihsan, leading to a nuanced ruling that depends on whether the hole is 'large' by the measure of three small toes. Within the school, there is further refinement on what constitutes 'three toes'—tips only or the entire toe.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling
The matn of al-Quduri sets the measure at three toes. Understand that this is the standard by which holes are judged.
The smallest toes are used for measurement out of caution.
2
Contrast the Opposing View
Zufr (within the Hanafi school) and al-Shafi'i argue that any hole, however small, invalidates masah. Their proof is qiyas: if washing the exposed part is required, then washing the entire foot is required, so masah cannot be valid.
This is the strict qiyas position.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi school responds with istihsan: khuffs customarily have small holes, so requiring removal for every small hole would cause hardship. Large holes are rare, so no hardship. Thus the measure of three small toes distinguishes between excusable and inexcusable holes.
The key principle: istihsan overrides qiyas here.
4
Map the Intra-Hanafi Spectrum
Within the Hanafi school, al-Sarakhsi held that even less than three toes prevents. Al-Halwani held that three complete toes (including the lower parts) must appear. The author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira declares al-Halwani's view as the most correct (al-ashah).
Also note: the big toe plus another can equal three small toes and prevent masah.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The preferred ruling: a hole must expose three complete small toes (tips and lower parts) to invalidate masah. If less, masah is valid. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Also consider location: holes above the ankle are irrelevant; holes that appear only while walking but not when stationary also invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين
و يبين منه مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصابع الرجل .
يروى : بالباء الموحدة، وبالثاء المثلثة، فالأول: في موضع، والثاني: في مواضع.
وفيه إشارة إلى أن الخروق تُجمع في خف واحد، ولا تُجمع في خفين بخلاف النجاسة المتفرقة ؛ لأنه حامل للكل.
وانكشاف العورة: نظير النجاسة.
وعند زفر، والشافعي): الخُرق اليسير يمنع المسح وإن قل؛ لأنه لما وجب غسل البادي: يجب غسل الباقي.
قلنا : الخفافُ لا تخلو عن يسيرِ خُرق عادةً، فيلحقه الحرج في النزع، وتخلو عن الكبير : فلا حرج.
والكبير : أن ينكشف منه مقدار ثلاث أصابع الرجل.

وفي المحيط : إذا كان يبدو قَدْرُ ثلاث أنامل، وأسافلُها مستورة: جاز.
وإن كان أقل من ذلك : جاز .
قال السرخسي : يمنع.
وقال الحلواني : لا يمنع حتى يبدو قدر ثلاث أصابع بكمالها، وهو الأصح، والأنامل هي رؤوس الأصابع.
فإن ظهرت الإبهام والأخرى معها مَنَعتا المسح؛ لأنهما يساويان الثلاث.
وفي مشكل القدوري : إذا كانت الإبهام مقدار ثلاث أصابع، وظهرت: لا تمنع.
وإذا كان مقطوع الأصابع : يُعتبر بأصابع غيره.
وكبر القدم: دليل على كبرها، وصغره: دليل على صغرها.
قوله: (وإن كان أقل من ذلك : جاز).
ولو كانت الأصابع تبدو من الخُرْق حالة المشي، ولا تبدو حال وضع القدم على الأرض لم يجز المسحُ عليه، وإن كان على العكس جاز. كذا في منية المصلي .
وهذا كله إذا كان الخُرق أسفل من الكعب، أما إذا كان فوقه: يجوز المسح عليه وإن كبر.
Chapter on wiping over khuffs. And it explains from it the amount of three toes of the foot. It is narrated: with the single dot ba', and with the three dots tha', the first in one place, the second in places. And in it there is an indication that holes are combined in one khuff, and not combined in two khuffs contrary to scattered impurity; because he carries the whole. And uncovering of the private parts is analogous to impurity. And according to Zufr and al-Shafi'i: a small hole prevents wiping even if it is small; because when washing the exposed part becomes obligatory, washing the rest becomes obligatory. We said: Khuffs are not free from small holes customarily, so hardship would follow in removing them, and they are free from large holes so no hardship. And the large [hole] is that from which the amount of three toes of the foot is exposed. His statement: (it explains from it the amount of three toes of the foot): meaning the smallest ones, that is correct; because the basis of the foot is the toes, considering that they are the origin of the foot, and the foot is subsidiary to them, and for this they said: Whoever cuts off the toes of a person's foot, the full blood-money is obligatory, and three [toes] are the most of them, so they stand in place of the whole, and the smallest is considered for caution. And in al-Muhit: If the amount of three fingertips [=tips of toes] appears, and their lower parts are covered, it is permissible. And if it is less than that, it is permissible. Al-Sarakhsi said: It prevents. And al-Halwani said: It does not prevent until the amount of three complete toes appears, and that is the most correct, and the fingertips are the heads of the [toes]. If the big toe and another appear with it, they prevent wiping because they equal three [small]. And in Mushkil al-Quduri: If the big toe is the size of three toes and appears, it does not prevent. And if one has amputated toes, he is measured by the toes of another. And the bigness of the foot is evidence of its [toes'] bigness, and its smallness is evidence of its smallness. His statement: (And if it is less than that, it is permissible). And if the toes appear from the hole while walking, and do not appear when placing the foot on the ground, wiping upon it is not permissible, and if the opposite is the case, it is permissible. Thus in Munyat al-Musalli. And all this is if the hole is below the ankle. As for if it is above it, wiping upon it is permissible even if it is large.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the permissible size of holes in khuffs for masah, with a brief inter-madhhab comparison with Zufr and al-Shafi'i. The chapter begins by stating that the measure is three toes from the foot. The author notes a variant reading of 'yabinu' with ba or tha, both meaning 'appears'. He explains that holes are combined in one khuff, not across two, unlike scattered impurity. Uncovering the awrah is similar to impurity. Zufr and al-Shafi'i argue that any small hole prevents wiping, because washing the exposed part obligates washing the rest by qiyas. The Hanafi response is that khuffs usually have small holes, so requiring removal would cause hardship, which is avoided by istihsan. Large holes, defined as exposing three small toes, are free from hardship, so they prevent wiping. The preferred opinion is that of al-Halwani: the hole must expose three complete toes (not just the tips), and the smallest toes are considered. Al-Sarakhsi holds that even less than that prevents, but the author declares al-Halwani's view as the most correct. The big toe counts as three small ones, so if it appears with another, it prevents. However, in Mushkil al-Quduri, a big toe the size of three does not prevent. For a person with amputated toes, the measure is based on average toes. Foot size indicates toe size. Additional conditions: if toes appear only while walking but not when stationary, wiping is not valid, but if they appear only when stationary, it is valid. If the hole is above the ankle, size does not matter.

Key Terms
خُرق (kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff that exposes the foot.
أصابع الرجل (asābi‘ al-rijl): The toes of the foot; specifically the smallest three toes are used as the measure.
أنامل (anāmil): Fingertips; here used metaphorically for the tips of the toes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position (al-Halwani), what size hole in the khuff prevents the validity of masah?
A) Any hole, no matter how small
B) A hole exposing three complete toes
C) A hole exposing the entire foot
D) A hole above the ankle

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, masah on khuffs remains valid for holes exposing less than three small toes; the most sound view requires three complete toes to appear.

Hole Size in Khuff: Dispute and Preferred Opinion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khuff hole size threshold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the minimum hole size that invalidates wiping over the khuff and distinguish it from the opposing view within the school.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff remains valid unless a hole exposes three full fingertips—smaller holes are ignored.

When a khuff (leather sock) develops a hole, the question arises: does the hole remove the dispensation of wiping? This passage presents a dispute between two Hanafi scholars—al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani—on the threshold. The commentator resolves the difference, giving us the preferred opinion still followed today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri states that a hole smaller than a certain size is permissible, but it does not specify the exact measure.
The base text uses 'أقل من ذلك' (less than that), leaving the threshold ambiguous.
2
State al-Sarakhsi's position
Al-Sarakhsi argues that any hole, no matter how small, prevents valid wiping.
His view is stricter, aiming for complete coverage.
3
State al-Halwani's position
Al-Halwani holds that only a hole exposing three complete fingertips (anamil) of the three middle fingers invalidates wiping.
This is the more lenient view.
4
Note the tarjih (preference)
The commentator declares al-Halwani's view as 'الأصح' (the most correct), making it the mufta bihi position.
Preference is based on practicality and ease.
5
Apply to edge cases
Additional rulings: thumb + another finger = three fingers; thumb alone if equal to three fingers does not prevent; for amputated persons measure with others' fingers; foot size indicates finger size.
These nuances come from later parts of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الثلاث.

Chapter of Wiping over Khuff. And if it (the hole) is less than that, it is permissible. (1) Al-Sarakhsi said: It prevents. And al-Halwani said: It does not prevent until the full measure of three fingers appears, and that is the most correct. And the 'anamal (finger joints) are the tips of the three fingers. Then if the thumb and another (finger) appear together, they prevent wiping because they are equal (in size to three fingers). And in 'Mushkil al-Quduri': If the thumb is the measure of three fingers and it appears, it does not prevent. And if one has amputated fingers, the standard is the fingers of others. And largeness of the foot is an indication of its largeness (of the fingers), and smallness is an indication of its smallness.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimum size of a hole in the khuff (leather sock) that prevents wiping over it. The base matn (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) states that if the hole is smaller than three fingers, wiping is permissible. The commentator then presents differing views: Al-Sarakhsi holds that any hole prevents wiping, while al-Halwani states that it only prevents if the hole exposes three complete fingertips (the anamil, i.e., the tips of the three middle fingers). The commentator declares al-Halwani's view as the most correct (al-ashah). Then a nuance: if the thumb and one other finger appear (which together equal the size of three small fingers), they do prevent wiping. However, according to 'Mushkil al-Quduri', if the thumb alone equals three fingers in size, it does not prevent. For a person with amputated fingers, the measure is taken from another person's fingers. Additionally, the size of the foot serves as an indicator of finger size: a large foot suggests larger fingers, etc. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that wiping is permissible unless three full fingertips are exposed.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or covering worn on the foot over which wiping (mash) is permitted during wudu.
أنملة (anmulah (pl. anamil)): The tip or joint of a finger; here specifically the topmost part of the three middle fingers used as a standard of measurement.
خرق (khurq): A hole or tear in the khuff; its size determines the validity of wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A hole that exposes three complete fingertips (anamil)
C) A hole that exposes the thumb and another finger
D) A hole larger than the foot

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that wiping over khuff remains valid unless a hole exposes three complete fingertips—smaller holes are tolerated.

Wiping over Khuffs: Timing of Hole Exposure and Position Relative to Ankle
Expansion of khuff hole rulings based on timing and ankle position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on wiping over a khuff when a hole exposes the foot only while walking, and distinguish between holes below and above the ankle.

Core Idea
If a hole exposes the foot only while walking, wiping is invalid; if only at rest, it is valid. Holes above the ankle never affect validity.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a small hole (less than three fingers) does not invalidate wiping. But what if the hole is only noticeable during movement? And does it matter where on the khuff the hole is located? This passage from Minyat al-Musalli provides crucial clarifications based on normal use and the requirement of covering the foot up to the ankle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios based on foot movement
Read the passage and note the two cases: (1) the toes appear from the hole during walking but not when the foot is at rest; (2) the toes appear at rest but not during walking.
The critical factor is when the foot is exposed during the typical action (walking).
2
Apply the ruling to each scenario
For scenario (1): wiping is not permissible because the hole is effectively open during normal use. For scenario (2): wiping is permissible because the hole is closed during walking, so the khuff is considered sufficiently covering.
The Hanafi principle: The state during walking (the primary use) determines validity.
3
Consider the position of the hole relative to the ankle
The passage adds that these rulings apply only when the hole is below the ankle (the ka'b). If the hole is above the ankle, wiping is permissible even if the hole is large.
The reason: the khuff is required to cover the foot including the ankle; the area above the ankle is not part of the essential covered area.
4
Recognize the authority and scope
This ruling is cited from Minyat al-Musalli, a later Hanafi work (fatawa mutakhkhirin). It is consistent with the general principle that the khuff must cover the foot adequately during normal use.
This is a mufta bihi position for many Hanafi muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن كان أقل من ذلك : جاز).
ولو كانت الأصابع تبدو من الخُرْق حالة المشي، ولا تبدو حال

And if the fingers appear from the hole during walking, but do not appear when the foot is placed on the ground, then wiping over it is not permissible. And if the opposite (i.e., appear at rest but not during walking), then it is permissible. Thus in 'Minyat al-Musalli' (2). And all this applies when the hole is below the ankle; but if it is above the ankle, then wiping over it is permissible even if it (the hole) is large.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the matn phrase 'وإن كان أقل من ذلك : جاز' (if it is less than that, it is permissible). It addresses two additional scenarios. First, if the hole only exposes the fingers during walking but not when the foot is at rest, then wiping is not valid because the hole is considered to be open during the act of walking, which is the normal use. Conversely, if the toes appear only when the foot is placed on the ground but not during walking, wiping is valid. Second, the commentator specifies that the previous rulings about hole size apply only when the hole is below the ankle (the ka'b). If the hole is above the ankle, the khuff is still valid for wiping even if the hole is large, because the area above the ankle is not a condition for the coverage of the khuff. This is based on the principle that the khuff must cover the foot including the ankle; holes above the ankle do not affect the required coverage.

Key Terms
خرق (khurq): A hole in the khuff that may expose the foot.
كعب (ka'b): The ankle bone; the point up to which the khuff must cover the foot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wiping is not permissible
B) Wiping is permissible
C) Wiping is permissible only if the hole is small
D) Wiping is not permissible if the hole is large

Key Takeaway
The validity of wiping over a khuff with a hole below the ankle depends on whether the foot is exposed during normal walking; holes above the ankle never invalidate wiping.

Conditions and Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuff
Lists conditions for valid khuff and what nullifies the wiping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a valid khuff and identify the nullifiers of the wiping state, including the prohibition for janabah.

Core Idea
The khuff must cover, fit, be walkable, and travel-worthy; wiping ends with wudu-breakers or removal.

Wiping over khuff is a concession in wudu, but it is not unconditional. The Hanafi school lays down specific requirements for the khuff itself and clarifies what breaks the wiping state. This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains both the conditions and the nullifiers, along with the reasoning for the janabah prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main prohibitions
First, note that wiping is not permissible for one in janabah. Second, note that it is permissible for minor impurity subject to conditions.
The passage begins with the absolute prohibition for janabah.
2
List the four conditions of the khuff
Extract each condition from the text: coverage of foot and ankle, proper fit (no empty front), possibility of continuous walking, and suitability for travel (linguistic distance).
The conditions are given with examples of what is excluded.
3
Analyze the proof for the janabah prohibition
The commentator provides a rationale: janabah does not recur frequently, so removal of khuff for ghusl is not burdensome.
This is a qiyas based on hardship and recurrence.
4
Identify the two categories of nullifiers
First, anything that nullifies wudu also nullifies the wiping. Second, removal of the khuff (after the first purification is broken) nullifies it.
The nullifiers are comprehensive; removal is a specific additional nullifier.

بعض الوضوء.
قوله: (وينقضه أيضا نزع الخف) : أي بعد انتقاض الطهارة الأولى؛
(1) أي السفر اللغوي، لا الشرعي، وهو مقدار فرسخ، أي ثلاثة أميال، وهي تعادل ٥ كم، وقد نبه إلى هذا ابن عابدين ۱۸۰/۲ فلينظر.
Chapter of Wiping over Khuff. And wiping over khuff is not permissible for the one upon whom ghusl (major purification) is obligatory. And that which nullifies wudu nullifies wiping over the khuff. And also removing the khuff nullifies it. And the conditions of the khuff upon which wiping is permissible: 1) It must cover the foot including the ankle; as a precaution against the torn one. 2) It must be occupied (worn) on the foot; as a precaution against the one with amputated fingers if he wears it and part of the front of the khuff becomes empty, then wiping over the empty part is not permissible. 3) That it is possible to walk continuously in it; as a precaution against making a khuff of iron, glass, or wood. 4) That walking distance of travel is cut off by it (i.e., it is suitable for travel); as a precaution against wrapping a rag around the legs: wiping over it is not permissible. Thus in 'al-Idah'. His saying: (And wiping is not permissible for the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory) because janabah (major impurity) does not normally recur, so there is no hardship in removal, unlike hadath (minor impurity), which recurs. Nullifiers of wiping over the khuff: His saying: (And everything that nullifies wudu nullifies wiping over the khuff) because it is part of wudu. His saying: (And also removal of the khuff nullifies it) meaning after the first purification (wudu) is nullified; (1) i.e., the linguistic travel, not the legal, which is the distance of a farsakh, i.e., three miles, which is equivalent to 5 km, and Ibn Abidin pointed this out in 2:180, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive statement of the conditions for a valid khuff that permits wiping, and the nullifiers of the wiping state. The commentator begins by stating that wiping is not permissible for someone in a state of major impurity (janabah), because janabah does not recur frequently, so removing the khuff for ghusl is not burdensome, unlike minor impurity (hadath) which recurs. Then nullifiers are stated: anything that nullifies wudu also nullifies the wiping (since wiping is a substitute for washing the feet in wudu), and additionally, removing the khuff nullifies it. Four conditions for the khuff are listed: (1) It must cover the foot including the ankle, to exclude torn ones. (2) It must be worn on the foot, so that if a person with amputated fingers wears it and part of the front is empty, wiping over the empty part is invalid. (3) It must be possible to walk continuously in it, excluding khuffs made of hard materials like iron, glass, or wood. (4) It must be of a type that can be walked in for a travel distance (linguistic travel, about 5 km), excluding rags wrapped around the foot. The footnote clarifies that the travel distance is the linguistic definition, not the legal definition for shortening prayers; it is about 5 km as per Ibn Abidin.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Major ritual purification required after sexual intercourse, menstruation, etc.
جنابة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
نزع (naz'): Removal of the khuff from the foot, which nullifies the wiping state after the first purification is broken.
مسافة السفر اللغوي (masafat al-safar al-lughawi): The linguistic definition of travel distance, about one farsakh (3 miles = 5 km), used as a condition for the khuff to be suitable for walking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for a khuff to be valid for wiping according to the passage?
A) It must cover the foot including the ankle
B) It must be made of leather
C) It must be possible to walk continuously in it
D) It must be suitable for travel of at least one farsakh

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuff requires the khuff to be covering, fitting, walkable, and travel-worthy; and it is nullified by wudu-breakers and removal.

The Ruling and Conditions for Wiping over Khuffs in Hanafi Fiqh
Chapter opening with prohibition for junub and conditions for khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on wiping over khuffs for a person in janabah, identify the nullifiers of the wiping state, and list the four conditions of the khuff according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a concession for wudu only, not for janabah, and the khuff must meet four specific conditions.

This passage opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs with a clear prohibition for those in major impurity. It then sets out what nullifies the wiping state and the conditions for valid khuffs. Understanding this distinction and conditions is essential for proper purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs during wudu. The ruling: it is permissible for wudu but absolutely prohibited for janabah (major impurity).
The prohibition for janabah is explicit in the text: 'لا يجوز المسح على الخفين لمن وجب عليه الغسل'.
2
Analyze the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The author provides a rational argument: janabah does not occur frequently, so there is no hardship in removing the khuff to wash the feet. In contrast, minor impurity occurs frequently, so the concession of wiping is granted to avoid hardship.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the ruling is based on the frequency of occurrence (ghalabah al-wujud).
3
List the nullifiers of the wiping state
Whatever nullifies wudu also nullifies the state of wiping. Additionally, removing the khuff and the expiry of the time period (1 day for resident, 3 days for traveler) nullify it.
The text says: 'وينقض المسح على الخفين ما ينقض الوضوء. وينقضه أيضاً نزع الخف، ومضي المدة.'
4
List and explain the four conditions of the khuff
1) Covers the foot including the ankle (not torn). 2) Worn properly so the entire foot is inside. 3) Allows normal walking (not made of iron, glass, or wood). 4) Enables travel distance (not a mere rag).
Each condition is illustrated with examples in the text to clarify.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on condition 4
There is disagreement on the definition of 'travel distance'. Some say the legal travel distance (3 days), others say the linguistic distance (a farsakh). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the linguistic travel distance (about 5 km), as noted in the commentary.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf does not affect the overall validity of the condition, only its measure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين ولا يجوز المسح على الخفين لمَن وَجَبَ عليه الغُسل . وينقض المسح على الخفين ما ينقض الوضوء. وينقضه أيضاً نَزْعُ الخف، ومضي المدة. وشرائط الخفا الذي يجوز المسح عليه: ۱ ـ أن يكون ساتراً للقدم مع الكعب؛ احترازاً عن المُخرَّق. ٢- وأن يكون مشغولاً بالرجل؛ احترازاً عن مقطوع الأصابع إذا لبسه وصار بعض الخف خالياً من مُقدَّمه ، فمَسَحَ على الخالي: لا يجوز. وأن يُمكن متابعة المشي فيه ؛ احترازاً مما إذا جَعَلَ له خفاً من حديد، أو زجاج، أو خشب. ٤- وأن تنقطع به مسافةُ السفر (۱) ؛ احترازاً عما إذا لف على رجليه خرقة : لا يجوز المسح عليها. كذا في «الإيضاح». * قوله: (ولا يجوز المسحُ لمن وجب عليه الغُسل)؛ لأن الجنابة لا تتكرر عادةً، فلا حرج في النزع، بخلاف الحدث، فإنه يتكرر.
Chapter of wiping over khuffs. It is not permissible to wipe over khuffs for one upon whom ghusl is obligatory. And wiping over khuffs is nullified by whatever nullifies wudu. It is also nullified by removing the khuff, and the passing of the time. And conditions of the khuff upon which wiping is permissible: 1. That it covers the foot including the ankle, as a precaution against the torn [khuff]. 2. That it is worn on the foot, as a precaution against the one with cut toes if he wears it and part of the khuff becomes empty in front, so he wipes on the empty part: it is not permissible. And that walking in it is possible, as a precaution against if he makes a khuff of iron, glass, or wood. 4. That the distance of traveling is covered by it, as a precaution against if he wraps a rag around his feet: it is not permissible to wipe over it. Likewise in al-Idah. * His statement: (It is not permissible to wipe for one upon whom ghusl is obligatory) because janabah does not usually repeat, so there is no hardship in removing [the khuff], unlike minor impurity, which repeats.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs with a clear restriction: wiping is not valid for someone in a state of major impurity (janabah). The commentator explains that this is because janabah is a rare occurrence, so removing the khuff to wash the feet is not a hardship. In contrast, minor impurity occurs frequently, so requiring removal would cause hardship. Thus, the permission to wipe over khuffs is limited to wudu. The passage then lists the nullifiers of the wiping state: anything that nullifies wudu, as well as the specific acts of removing the khuff or the expiry of the time period. Finally, it enumerates four conditions for the khuff itself: it must cover the foot including the ankle (not torn), be properly worn (so that the entire foot is covered), allow walking (not made of hard materials), and enable travel (not a mere rag). Each condition is illustrated with examples to clarify the ruling. The commentary on the first condition references 'الإيضاح' as a source.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or boot worn over the foot, used for wiping during wudu.
مسح (mash): Wiping, specifically passing wet hand over a limb or a khuff as part of purification.
نقض (naqd): Nullification or invalidation of the state of purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following nullifies the state of wiping over khuffs specifically (not just nullifying wudu)?
A) Eating
B) Removing the khuff
C) Touching the opposite gender
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a concession limited to wudu, with strict conditions on both the act and the khuff itself.

Nullification of Wiping by Removal of Khuffs
Commentary on the nullification of wiping by removal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that nullify wiping upon removal of the khuff and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on partial removal.

Core Idea
Removing most or all of the foot from the khuff nullifies the wiping; the correct view is that exiting most of the foot suffices.

Wiping over khuffs is a valid concession (rukhsa) in the Hanafi school, but it is nullified by certain actions. One specific nullifier is physically removing the khuff. But what if only part of the foot comes out? This lesson explores the threshold for nullification and an important difference between Imam Muhammad and the majority of Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nullifier
The text states that wiping is nullified by anything that nullifies wudu, and also by the action of removing the khuff. The removal nullifies only after hadath (impurity) has occurred, because the khuff acts as a barrier preventing the hadath from reaching the foot.
2
Determine the extent of removal
The commentator explains that the nullification occurs when the foot exits to the shin (i.e., completely) or by most of the foot. The phrase 'أكثر القدم' (most of the foot) is the correct criterion.
This is the mufta bihi position (الصحيح).
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad holds that if at least three fingers of the back of the foot remain within the area of wiping, the wiping remains valid. This is based on the idea that the place of the obligatory act (محل الفرض) is still present.
This view is not the relied-upon one (الصحيح prevails).
4
Understand the rationale
The nullification occurs because the removal of the barrier (khuff) allows the hadath to reach the foot. The foot is now exposed, so the previous wiping is no longer valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نواقض المسح على الخفين :] * قوله: (وينقض المسح على الخفين كلُّ شيء ينقض الوضوء)؛ لأنه بعض الوضوء. قوله: (وينقضه أيضا نزع الخف) : أي بعد انتقاض الطهارة الأولى؛ لسراية الحدث إلى القدم لزوال المانع، وهو الخف. وحكم النزع يثبت بخروج القدم إلى الساق، وكذا بأكثر القدم، وهو الصحيح. وعن محمد: إذا بقي قدرُ ثلاث أصابع من ظهر القدم في محل المسح : بقي حكم المسح ؛ لبقاء محل الفرض في مستقره. قوله : (ومضي المدة)؛ لسراية الحدث إلى القدم. وكذا نَزْعُ أحد الخفين. قوله : ومضي المدة: هذا إذا وجد الماء، أما إذا لم يجده: لم ينتقض مسحه، بل تجوز له الصلاة، حتى إذا انقضت وهو في الصلاة، ولم يجد ماء فإنه يمضي على صلاته ؛ لأن حاجته هنا إلى غسل رجليه. فلو قطع الصلاة: فإنه يتيمم، ولا حظ للرجلين في التيمم، فلهذا كان المضي على صلاته أولى. ومن المشايخ من قال : تفسد صلاته، والأول أصح.. وكذلك إذا مضت المدة، وكان يخاف الضرر من البرد إذا نزعهما : جاز له أن يصلي. كذا في «الذخيرة». ولو كان الخف ذا طاقين، فمسح عليه، ثم نزع أحد طاقيه: فإنه لا يجب عليه إعادة المسح على ما ظهر تحته.
Nullifiers of wiping over khuffs: ] * His statement: (Wiping over khuffs is nullified by everything that nullifies wudu) because it is part of wudu. His statement: (It is also nullified by removing the khuff) that is, after the nullification of the first purity, due to the transmission of the hadath to the foot by the removal of the barrier, which is the khuff. The ruling of removal is established by the foot coming out to the shin, and likewise by most of the foot, and this is the correct view. From Muhammad: if there remains the extent of three fingers of the back of the foot in the place of wiping, the ruling of wiping remains due to the remaining of the place of the obligatory act in its place. His statement: (And the passing of the time) due to the transmission of the hadath to the foot. And likewise the removal of one of the two khuffs. His statement: And the passing of the time: this is when water is found, but if he does not find it, his wiping is not nullified, rather his prayer is permitted for him, such that if the time expires while he is in prayer and he does not find water, then he proceeds with his prayer because his need here is to wash his feet. If he cuts the prayer, he would perform tayammum, and feet have no role in tayammum, so proceeding with his prayer is preferable. And some of the mashayikh said: his prayer is invalid, but the first is more correct. Similarly, if the time expires and he fears harm from the cold if he removes them, it is permissible for him to pray. Likewise in al-Dhakhira. And if the khuff has two layers, and he wipes over it, then removes one layer, it is not necessary for him to repeat the wiping over what appeared beneath it.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed rules for what nullifies the state of wiping over khuffs. The commentator begins by stating that any act that nullifies wudu also nullifies the wiping, because the wiping is part of the wudu process. Then he addresses the unique nullifier: physical removal of the khuff. This causes the hadath (impurity) to immediately reach the foot because the barrier is gone. The ruling is that if the entire foot or most of it comes out, the wiping is nullified. However, Imam Muhammad reports a view that if at least three fingers of the back of the foot remain within the wiping area, the wiping remains valid. The correct position (الصحيح) is that the vast majority of the foot must be out. Next, the passage discusses the expiry of the wiping period. This nullifies the wiping only if water is available. If water is not found, the wiping continues to be valid, and one can even continue praying after the period ends if water is absent. This is based on the necessity of washing the feet, which cannot be done without water. If one cuts the prayer to seek water, they would have to perform tayammum, which does not involve the feet, so it is better to continue the prayer. There is disagreement among later scholars on whether the prayer becomes invalid, but the preferred view is that it remains valid. Finally, an exceptional case is mentioned: if a khuff has two layers and one is removed, there is no need to repeat the wiping over the remaining layer, because the act of wiping was valid and the removal of a layer does not necessitate repetition.

Key Terms
نزع (naz'): Removal of the khuff from the foot, which nullifies the state of wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, when does removing the khuff nullify the wiping?
A) When the entire foot exits.
B) When most of the foot exits.
C) When any part of the foot exits.
D) When the khuff is removed for more than an hour.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi view is that removal of the khuff nullifies the wiping when most of the foot exits, not necessarily the entire foot.

Expiry of the Wiping Period and Exceptional Cases
Commentary on expiry of the wiping period and related exceptional rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when the expiry of the wiping period nullifies the state of wiping and when it does not, including the concession for lack of water and fear of cold.

Core Idea
Expiry of the period only nullifies wiping if water is available; if not, the wiping remains valid and prayer can continue.

The permission to wipe over khuffs is limited to one day and night for residents and three for travelers. But what happens when the time expires? Does the wiping automatically become null? This lesson reveals that the nullification depends on the availability of water. Additionally, we explore special cases: when water is absent during prayer, fear of cold, and the ruling on multi-layered khuffs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule
The passing of the prescribed period (muddah) nullifies the wiping, as stated in the text. The hadath is considered to have reached the foot after the time expires.
This applies when water is available.
2
Consider the exceptional case of no water
If the period expires and no water is found, the wiping is not nullified. The person can continue to pray, even if the expiration occurs during prayer. Proceeding with prayer is preferred over cutting it to perform tayammum, because tayammum does not involve washing the feet.
This is a concession (rukhsa) to avoid hardship.
3
Note the disagreement among later scholars
Some later scholars (mashayikh) said that the prayer becomes invalid upon expiry, but the preferred view (الأول أصح) is that it remains valid.
4
Examine the cold weather concession
If the period expires and removing the khuffs would cause harm due to extreme cold, it is permissible to pray without removing them, even if water is available. This is recorded in al-Dhakhira.
5
Apply to multi-layered khuffs
If a khuff has two layers (طاقين) and one layer is removed after wiping, there is no need to repeat the wiping over the remaining layer. The initial wiping remains valid.
This shows the legal principle: the wiping covers all layers as long as the outermost was wiped.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Takeaway
Expiry of the wiping period only nullifies wiping if water is present; if water is absent, the wiping remains valid due to the concession of necessity.

Nullification of Wiping over Khuffs: When Period Ends or Khuff Removed
Commentary on rulings when the wiping period ends or khuff is removed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the wiping period ends or the khuff is removed, apply the exception when water is unavailable, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
When the barrier (khuff) is removed or the period ends, only the feet need washing; the rest of wudu remains intact.

This lesson examines the rulings that nullify the validity of wiping over khuffs—specifically when the permitted period expires or the khuff is removed. The passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah also addresses special cases: when water is absent, when cold weather poses a danger, and when the khuff has two layers. We will work through these scenarios and the Hanafi position, noting the disagreement with al-Shafi'i and the internal Hanafi nuance from Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nullifying events
Two events nullify the wipe: (1) the passing of the permitted period (for a resident: one day and night; for a traveler: three days and nights), and (2) removing the khuff (naz'). Understand why each nullifies: because the barrier is gone, the prior impurity spreads to the foot.
The text emphasizes that removal of most of the foot (akthar al-qadam) counts as full removal.
2
Determine the required action after nullification
When the period ends or the khuff is removed, the required action is: remove the khuffs, wash the feet, and pray. No need to repeat the entire wudu. This is the Hanafi position.
The phrase 'ليس عليه إعادة بقية الوضوء' is a qualification against al-Shafi'i.
3
Apply the exception: water unavailable
If the period ends but no water is found, the wipe is not nullified; it remains valid. The person may continue or start prayer without tayammum, because tayammum does not involve the feet. If already in prayer, he continues.
Some mashayikh said the prayer is invalid, but the text holds the first view as more correct.
4
Consider additional scenarios
(a) Fear of cold: if removing the khuff would cause harm, it is permissible to pray without washing the feet. (b) Two-layered khuff: if one wipes over the outer layer and then removes it, no need to repeat wiping on the inner layer. (c) Muhammad's view: if three fingers of the top of the foot remain within the wiping area, the wipe persists.
Muhammad's view is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the majority holds that removal of most of the foot nullifies.
5
Contrast with other schools
Al-Shafi'i requires repeating the entire wudu after the period ends. Ibn Abi Layla requires nothing. The Hanafi position is that only foot washing is needed—a middle view based on the reasoning that the impurity only spread to the feet.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: Hanafis save time and water by not repeating the full wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين
قول : (ومضي المدة)؛ لسراية الحدث إلى القدم لزوال المانع، وهو الخف.
وحكم النزع يثبت بخروج القدم إلى الساق، وكذا بأكثر القدم، وهو الصحيح. وعن محمد: إذا بقي قدرُ ثلاث أصابع من ظهر القدم في محل المسح : بقي حكم المسح ؛ لبقاء محل الفرض في مستقره.
قول : ومضي المدة: هذا إذا وجد الماء، أما إذا لم يجده: لم ينتقض مسحه، بل تجوز له الصلاة، حتى إذا انقضت وهو في الصلاة، ولم يجد ماء فإنه يمضي على صلاته ؛ لأن حاجته هنا إلى غسل رجليه. فلو قطع الصلاة: فإنه يتيمم، ولا حظ للرجلين في التيمم، فلهذا كان المضي على صلاته أولى. ومن المشايخ من قال : تفسد صلاته، والأول أصح..
وكذلك إذا مضت المدة، وكان يخاف الضرر من البرد إذا نزعها : جاز له أن يصلي. كذا في «الذخيرة».
ولو كان الخف ذا طاقين، فمسح عليه، ثم نزع أحد طاقيه: فإنه لا يجب عليه إعادة المسح على ما ظهر تحته.
باب المسح على الخفين
فإذا تمت المدة : نَزَع خَفَّيْه، وغَسَلَ رِجليه، وصلَّى، وليس عليه إعادة بقية الوضوء .
قوله : (فإذا تمت المدة : نَزَعَ خفيه، وغَسَلَ رجليه، وصلى). وكذا إذا نزع قبل مضي المدة ؛ لأنه عند النزع يسري الحدث السابق إلى القدمين، فكأنه لم يغسلهما.
* قوله: (وليس عليه إعادة بقية الوضوء).
هذا احتراز عن قول الشافعي) ، فإنه يقول: عليه إعادة الوضوء.
وقال ابن أبي ليلى: لا يعيد شيئاً من الوضوء.
Chapter: Wiping over khuffs. Statement: (And the passing of the period); because the prior impurity spreads to the foot due to the removal of the barrier, which is the khuff. And the ruling of removal is established by the foot exiting to the shin, and likewise by most of the foot, and this is correct. And from Muhammad: if the amount of three fingers of the top of the foot remain in the place of wiping, the ruling of wiping remains; because the place of the obligation remains in its original position. Statement: And the passing of the period: this is when he finds water, but if he does not find it: his wiping is not nullified, rather his prayer is permissible for him, such that when it ends while he is in prayer and he does not find water, he continues his prayer; because his need here is to wash his feet. For if he cuts the prayer, he would perform tayammum, and there is no share for the feet in tayammum, so continuing his prayer is preferable. Some mashayikh said: his prayer is invalidated; but the first is more correct. Likewise, if the period passes and he fears harm from cold if he removes them, it is permissible for him to pray. So in al-Dhakhirah. And if the khuff has two layers, so he wiped over it, then removed one of its layers: then it is not obligatory upon him to repeat the wiping on what appears beneath it. Chapter: Wiping over khuffs. Then when the period ends: he removes his two khuffs, washes his feet, and prays, and upon him is not repetition of the rest of the wudu. His statement: (Then when the period ends: he removes his two khuffs, washes his feet, and prays). And likewise if he removes before the passing of the period; because at the time of removal the prior impurity spreads to the two feet, so it is as if he did not wash them. *His statement: (And upon him is not repetition of the rest of the wudu). This is a qualification against the statement of al-Shafi'i, for he says: upon him is repetition of wudu. And Ibn Abi Layla said: he does not repeat anything of wudu.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah on Mukhtasar al-Quduri regarding the rulings that nullify the validity of wiping over the khuff (leather socks). The commentary opens by stating that the passing of the assigned period nullifies the wipe because the original impurity (hadath) spreads to the foot once the barrier (the khuff) is effectively removed. The same ruling applies when the khuff is removed: wiping becomes invalid because the foot is exposed and the previous state of impurity returns. However, Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani adds a nuance: if at least three fingers of the top of the foot remain within the wiping area, the ruling of the wipe persists because the place of the obligation (the foot) is still largely covered. The commentary then addresses the scenario when the period ends but water is unavailable: the wipe is not nullified, and it is permissible to continue prayer. If the prayer is interrupted and he performs tayammum, there is no benefit for the feet in tayammum, so continuing the prayer is preferable. Some later scholars argued that the prayer becomes invalid, but the first view is the relied-upon position. Furthermore, if the period ends and there is fear of harm from cold water, it is permissible to pray without washing the feet (preserving the khuff). The case of a two-layered khuff is also addressed: if one wipes over it and then removes an outer layer, it is not necessary to repeat the wipe on the inner layer. The commentary then returns to the basic ruling: when the period ends (or when the khuff is removed before the period), one must remove the khuffs, wash the feet, and pray; there is no need to repeat the entire wudu. This last point distinguishes the Hanafi view from al-Shafi'i, who required a full wudu renewal. Ibn Abi Layla held that nothing at all is repeated. The Hanafi position (as per this text) is that only the foot washing is required, not the entire wudu.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock worn over the foot, which may be wiped during wudu under specific conditions.
مضي المدة (madiyy al-mudda): The expiration of the allowed period for wiping (for residents: one day and night; for travelers: three days and nights).
النزع (al-naz'): Removing the khuff, which nullifies the wipe because the barrier is gone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Perform tayammum and pray.
B) Remove the khuffs, wash the feet, and pray without repeating the rest of wudu.
C) Repeat the entire wudu from the beginning.
D) Continue praying without any action.

Key Takeaway
When the wiping period ends or khuff is removed, only the feet need washing; the rest of the wudu remains intact.

The Resident-Traveler Wipe Period: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on whether a resident-traveler completes a longer wipe period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the wipe period for a resident who travels before completing a day and night, identify the Shafi'i objection, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When a resident travels before a day, Hanafi law extends his wipe to three days — a leniency Shafi'i rejects.

This passage addresses a classic conflict between continuity of a ritual act and change of legal status. The Hanafi school, emphasizing the initial start of the act, allows the traveler's longer wipe period. The Shafi'i school, focusing on the current status, restricts it. Understanding this dispute reveals how each school weights different factors in rulings tied to time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario: a person begins wiping over khuffs as a resident (so allowed one day and night), then travels before completing that one day and night. What should his wipe period be?
The starting premise is clear in the text.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the matn, he wipes 'the completion of three days and their nights' — i.e., the traveler's full three-day period from the start of his wipe.
This is the Hanafi position.
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i is quoted as saying it is not permissible for him to wipe the wipe of a traveler. He likely requires the travel to coincide with the entire period.
The text cuts off before giving the Hanafi response.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The text begins to articulate a principle: 'what is considered with us in rulings related to time...' but ends. In full, the Hanafi principle would likely state that for time-bound rulings, the governing status is that at the beginning of the time (or at the start of the act).
This principle is not fully quoted; it is inferred from Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Hanafi, the person can wipe for three days; under Shafi'i, only one day, so after a day he must remove the khuffs and wash his feet for subsequent prayers.
This is the real-world consequence of the different rulings.

This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the length of the wiping period when a person starts wiping as a resident (i.e., allowed one day and night) but then travels before that first day and night is completed. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that such a person can continue to wipe for the full traveler's period (three days and three nights) from the time he began his original wipe. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that it is not permissible for him to adopt the traveler's period in this case. The commentary then begins to explain the underlying principle: 'what is considered with us in rulings related to time...' but the text cuts off. The complete principle would likely be that in the Hanafi school, the relevant factor for determining the wipe period is the status at the time of the first wipe or at the completion of the period? This is a known discussion: for rulings tied to time, the governing condition at the start of the time may be considered. The full articulation would clarify why the traveler's period applies.

تمام يوم وليلة (tamam yawm wa layla): The duration of one full day and night that must pass before travel can affect the wipe period according to this dispute.
