Maximum Duration and Colors of Menstruation
Ruling on maximum hayd and colors, with intra-Hanafi dispute on kudrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum duration of menstruation according to the Hanafi school, identify which colors are considered menstruation, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding muddy discharge (kudrah) at the beginning of the period.

Core Idea
Any discharge—red, yellow, or muddy—within the ten-day menstrual period is considered menstruation; but Abu Yusuf excludes muddy discharge at the very start.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses two key determinations in menstrual fiqh: the maximum length of hayd and the colors that qualify as menstruation. Understanding these rulings is essential for a woman to correctly identify her menstrual days and distinguish them from istihadah. The text also presents a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement: the status of muddy discharge (kudrah) when it appears at the very beginning of the period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
First, determine the two main legal determinations: (1) the maximum duration of hayd is ten days; (2) any discharge (red, yellow, muddy) within those days is hayd. Note the evidence: a hadith stating the maximum.
This is the general Hanafi position from the matn.
2
State the majority Hanafi position on kudrah
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) hold that if a woman sees kudrah at any point during the menstrual period—beginning, middle, or end—it is considered hayd. This is based on the principle that any discharge in the period is menstrual.
The text uses 'عندهما' indicating agreement of the two.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's opposing view and his proof
Abu Yusuf argues that kudrah is hayd only if it occurs at the end of the period, after clear blood has appeared. His reasoning: kudrah typically follows clear blood; if it appears at the start, it is not following a pattern, so it should not be counted as hayd.
His proof is based on customary observation (urf).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and determine the mufta bihi
The text does not explicitly refute Abu Yusuf but presents his view as a minority. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, because it is safer and consistent with the general principle.
Tarjih authority: the text's phrasing 'cindahuma' indicates the dominant position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference matters when a woman experiences only kudrah at the start of her period without any red blood. Under Abu Hanifa, she begins her hayd count from day one; under Abu Yusuf, she does not enter hayd until she sees clear blood.
This affects rulings on prayer, fasting, and marital intimacy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكثر الحيض عشرة أيام ولياليها، وما زاد على ذلك : فهو استحاضة. وما تراه المرأة من الحُمرة، والصفرة والكدرة في أيام الحيض : فهو حيض. : قوله: (وأكثره: عشرة أيام ولياليها لما روينا، (وما زاد على ذلك فهو استحاضة). * قوله: (وما تراه المرأةُ من الحُمْرة، والصفرة، والكدرة في مدة الحيض : فهو حيض). سواء رأت الكدرة في أول أيامها، أو في آخرها: فهو حيض عندهما، تقدمت أو تأخرت. وقال أبو يوسف إن رأتها في أول أيامها: لم تكن حيضاً، وإن رأتها في آخر أيامها : كانت حيضاً. فهي عنده لا تكون حيضاً إلا إذا تأخرت؛ لأن خروج الكدرة يتأخر عن الصافي، فإذا تقدمها دم أمكن جعلها حيضاً تبعاً، وأما إذا لم يتقدمها دم، فلو جعلناها حيضاً: كانت متبوعةً، لا تبعاً. (۱) سنن الدارقطني، وضعفه، وكذلك ابن حجر في الدراية ٨٤/١، وينظر نصب الراية ۱۹۱/۱ فقد ذكر له طرقاً عديدة، وشواهد كثيرة.
And the maximum of menstruation is ten days and their nights, and what exceeds that is istihadah. And whatever a woman sees of redness, yellowness, and muddiness during the days of menstruation is menstruation. His statement: 'And its maximum is ten days and their nights' due to what we narrated, 'and what exceeds that is istihadah.' His statement: 'And whatever a woman sees of redness, yellowness, and muddiness during the menstrual period is menstruation.' Whether she sees muddiness at the beginning of her days or at the end, it is menstruation according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) whether it precedes or follows. Abu Yusuf said: if she sees it at the beginning of her days, it is not menstruation, but if she sees it at the end of her days, it is menstruation. So according to him, it is not menstruation except if it occurs later, because the emission of muddiness comes after clear blood; if blood precedes it, it is possible to consider it menstruation as a follower, but if no blood precedes it, if we were to consider it menstruation, it would be a leader, not a follower.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on menstruation, covering the maximum duration and the status of different colors. First, the maximum is ten days; anything beyond is istihadah. The hadith from al-Daraqutni is cited as proof. Then the ruling on colors: red, yellow, and muddy discharges seen within the menstrual period are all considered menstruation. This is based on the principle that any discharge during the possible time is menstrual. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding muddy discharge (kudrah) at the beginning of the period. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is menstruation regardless of whether it appears at the start or end. Abu Yusuf disagrees: if it appears at the beginning (before any clear blood), it is not menstruation because it is not preceded by pure blood that would make it a follower; if it appears at the end, it is menstruation as a follower. The reasoning is that muddy discharge typically comes after clear blood, so when it precedes, it does not have the usual pattern. The footnote provides the source and scholarly critique of the hadith.

Key Terms
الحُمرة (al-humrah): Reddish discharge; a type of blood that is clearly menstrual.
الصفرة (al-sufrah): Yellowish discharge; considered menstrual if within the period.
الكدرة (al-kudrah): Muddy, turbid discharge; its status depends on timing and the imam's view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, when is muddy discharge (kudrah) considered menstruation?
A) Always, if it occurs within the menstrual period
B) Only if it appears at the beginning of the period
C) Only if it appears at the end of the period
D) Never, it is always istihadah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, any colored discharge (red, yellow, muddy) within the ten-day menstrual period is menstruation; the majority holds that muddy discharge at the very beginning counts, while Abu Yusuf requires it to appear after clear blood.

Maximum Duration of Menstruation
Ruling with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the maximum duration of menstruation and identify the hadith proof on which it is based.

Core Idea
Menstruation in the Hanafi school is defined by a maximum of ten days; blood beyond that is irregular bleeding (istihadah).

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah establishes a key legal boundary in the chapter of menstruation. It states that any blood beyond ten days is not considered menstrual, regardless of its color or quantity, and thus the woman is legally treated as mustahadah with different ritual obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: it states that the maximum of hayd is ten days and nights. Any blood beyond that is istihadah. This is a clear legal limit.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as proof: 'The minimum of menstruation is three days, and its maximum is ten days.' Note that this hadith is considered weak by some scholars, but the Hanafi school relies on it.
The phrase 'لما روينا' indicates the Hanafi tradition accepts this hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly provides numerical limits. The Hanafi school uses these numbers as definitive legal criteria, establishing the maximum as ten days.
The hadith's meaning (dalalah) is clear and decisive (qati), even though its transmission (thubut) is zanni.
4
Apply the ruling
If a woman bleeds for eleven days or more, only the first ten days count as hayd. The remaining days are istihadah, requiring her to pray and fast, but with wudu for each prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحيض
وأكثر الحيض عشرة أيام ولياليها، وما زاد على ذلك : فهو استحاضة.
عليه الصلاة والسلام : «أقل الحيض ثلاثة أيام، وأكثره: عشرة أيام».
قوله: (وأكثره: عشرة أيام ولياليها لما روينا، (وما زاد على ذلك فهو استحاضة).
Chapter of Menstruation. The maximum of menstruation is ten days and their nights, and what exceeds that is istihadah. Upon him be peace and blessings: 'The minimum of menstruation is three days, and its maximum is ten days.' His saying: (And its maximum is ten days and their nights because we narrated, and what exceeds that is istihadah).
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Sharh. The matn (base text) states the maximum duration of menstruation is ten days and nights; any blood beyond that is istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding). The commentator then cites a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as proof: 'The minimum of menstruation is three days, and its maximum is ten days.' Although this hadith is considered weak by some hadith scholars, the Hanafi school relies on it (مما روينا) as a basis for this ruling. The phrase 'قوله' refers back to the matn, and the commentator reaffirms the ruling.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual blood that occurs within the recognized duration (minimum 3, maximum 10 days) and has specific colors.
استحاضة (istihadah): Non-menstrual bleeding that exceeds the maximum duration of hayd (10 days) or occurs outside the normal cycle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on blood that exceeds ten days and nights?
A) It is still hayd until it stops.
B) It is istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding).
C) It is considered as hayd only if it is red.
D) It requires a sacrifice (dam).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes the maximum duration of menstruation at ten days and nights, beyond which blood is considered istihadah.

Brown Discharge at Menstrual Onset: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on colors of blood and disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi ruling on brown discharge (kudrah) during menstruation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding its status at the beginning of the period.

Core Idea
Brown discharge at the start of menstruation is hayd by majority; Abu Yusuf says it is hayd only if preceded by red blood.

This lesson examines the ruling on brownish discharge (kudrah) during menstruation. While all three Hanafi imams agree that red and yellow are hayd, a subtle disagreement exists between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on whether kudrah at the beginning of the period counts as menstruation. The issue hinges on the legal unity of the menstrual duration and a physical understanding of cervical anatomy.

Guided Path
1
Identify common ground
State the agreed-upon rule: any discharge (red, yellow, brown) during the days of menstruation is hayd. Note that the disagreement is only about brown discharge at the very beginning.
All three imams agree on red and yellow; the dispute is specific to kudrah.
2
State the point of disagreement
Abu Yusuf holds that kudrah at the beginning without prior red blood is not hayd, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is hayd regardless of timing.
The majority ('indahuma') refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that kudrah is a residual discharge that normally follows clear blood. If it appears first, it would be primary (متبوعة) rather than secondary (تبعاً), so it cannot be hayd.
His analogy is based on the natural order of discharge.
4
Analyze the majority response
The majority responds: the entire menstrual period is one continuous duration; if kudrah at the end is hayd, so is kudrah at the beginning, like redness. They also refute the anatomical assumption: the cervix is inverted, so kudrah can exit first, like sediment from a jar with a bottom hole.
This rebuttal uses qiyas jaliy with the jar analogy.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to Abu Yusuf, a woman seeing only brown discharge at the start would not consider it hayd and would continue acts of worship; according to the majority, she would stop.
The thamarah al-khilaf affects prayer and fasting obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما تراه المرأة من الحُمرة، والصفرة والكدرة في أيام الحيض : فهو حيض.
سواء رأت الكدرة في أول أيامها، أو في آخرها: فهو حيض عندهما، تقدمت أو تأخرت.
وقال أبو يوسف إن رأتها في أول أيامها: لم تكن حيضاً، وإن رأتها في آخر أيامها : كانت حيضاً.
فهي عنده لا تكون حيضاً إلا إذا تأخرت؛ لأن خروج الكدرة يتأخر عن الصافي، فإذا تقدمها دم أمكن جعلها حيضاً تبعاً، وأما إذا لم يتقدمها دم، فلو جعلناها حيضاً: كانت متبوعةً، لا تبعاً.
وهما يقولان ما كان حيضاً في آخر أيامها: كان حيضاً في أول أيامها، كالحمرة؛ لأن جميع مدة الحيض في حكم واحد.
وما قاله أبو يوسف إن خروج الكدرة يتأخر عن الصافي: إنما هو فيما إذا كان مخرجه من أعلاه، أما إذا كان من أسفله: فالكدرة تخرج قبل الصافي، وهنا المخرج من أسفل ؛ لأن فم الرحم منكوس، فتخرج الكدرة أولاً، كالجَرَّة إذا ثُقب أسفلها.
And what a woman sees of redness, yellowness, and brownness during the days of menstruation: it is hayd. Whether she sees brownness at the beginning of her days or at their end: it is hayd according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), whether it precedes or follows. Abu Yusuf said: If she sees it at the beginning of her days, it is not hayd, but if she sees it at the end of her days, it is hayd. So according to him, it is not hayd unless it is delayed; because the exit of brownness is delayed from the clear blood, so if blood precedes it, it is possible to make it hayd as a follower. But if blood does not precede it, if we make it hayd, it would be a followed, not a follower. They (the two) say: What was hayd at the end of her days was hayd at the beginning of her days, like redness; because all the period of menstruation is in one ruling. And what Abu Yusuf said that the exit of brownness is delayed from the clear: that is only when its exit is from its top; but if from its bottom, the brownness comes out before the clear, and here the exit is from the bottom because the mouth of the uterus is inverted, so the brownness comes out first, like a jar if its bottom is punctured.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that any discharge of red, yellow, or brown (kudrah) during the days of menstruation is considered hayd. The commentary explains that according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (عندهما), this applies regardless of whether the brownness appears at the beginning or end of the period. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: if brownness appears at the beginning without prior red blood, it is not hayd, but if it appears at the end after red blood, it is hayd. His reasoning is that brownness is normally a residual discharge that follows clear blood; if it comes first, it cannot be considered hayd because it would be primary rather than secondary. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that the entire menstrual period is one continuous legal duration; if brownness at the end is hayd, then at the beginning it should also be hayd, just like redness. They further refute Abu Yusuf's anatomical assumption by noting that the cervical canal is inverted (mouth of uterus is downward), so brownness can emerge first, analogous to a jar with a hole at the bottom where sediment comes out first.

Key Terms
كدرة (kudrah): Brownish or murky discharge that is not pure red or yellow; its classification as hayd depends on timing and presence of prior blood.
عندهما (indahuma): According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani), indicating the majority view within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, when is brown discharge (kudrah) considered menstruation?
A) Only if it appears at the end of the period after red blood.
B) Always, regardless of timing.
C) Only if it appears at the beginning.
D) Never, as it is always istihadah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, brown discharge during menstrual days is considered hayd by the majority, and Abu Yusuf's opposing view is rebutted with the unity of the menstrual period and cervical anatomy.

Sign of Purity from Hayd and Dropping of Prayer
Ruling on the sign of purity from hayd and the effect on prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for the end of menstruation (hayd) and explain why the obligation of prayer is dropped during hayd, citing the concept of hardship (haraj).

Core Idea
A menstruating woman is not pure until she sees white discharge; prayer is obligatory in principle but dropped due to hardship.

This passage addresses two linked rulings: the sign that marks the end of menstruation, and the effect of menstruation on the obligation of prayer. The Hanafi school insists on a clear physical indicator—pure white discharge—before a woman may resume worship. The commentary also raises a subtle usul point: was the obligation of prayer ever present for a menstruating woman? Abu Zayd al-Dabusi clarifies that it was, but is lifted due to hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage contains two distinct rulings: (1) the criterion for the end of hayd, and (2) the lifting of the prayer obligation during hayd.
Both are interconnected but separate legal issues.
2
Understand the criterion for purity
The text states 'until she sees pure whiteness' (البياض الخالص). The commentary explains this as either a mucus-like discharge or the result of a cotton test. The key is that mere cessation of bleeding is insufficient; a positive sign of purity is required.
This is stricter than some other schools.
3
Grasp the obligation status of prayer
The phrase 'the prayer drops from the menstruating woman' implies that prayer was originally obligatory upon her, then removed. The commentator notes this indicates prior obligation.
This is a rukhsah (concession).
4
Appreciate the usul argument
Abu Zayd al-Dabusi argues that rulings of obligation are established on all humans (including minors, insane, and menstruating women) but are dropped due to hardship (haraj). He cites the example of land tax (ushr and kharaj) which is universally owed.
This reinforces that the woman is addressed by the command but excused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى ترى البياض الخالص .
قيل : هو شيء يُشبه المخاط يخرج عند انتهاء الحيض. وقيل: هو القطن الذي تختبر به المرأةُ نفسها، إذا خرج أبيض: فقد طهرت.
والحيض يُسقط عن الحائض الصلاة.
فيه إشارة إلى أنها وجبت عليها الصلاة، ثم سقطت.
وهذه المسألة اختلف فيها الأصوليون، وهي أن الأحكام هل هي ثابتة على الصبي، والمجنون، والحائض، أم لا؟
فاختار أبو زيد الدبوسي أنها ثابتةٌ، والسقوط بعذر الحرج، قال: لأن الآدمي أصل لوجوب الحقوق عليه ألا ترى أن عليه عشر أرضه وخراجها، بالإجماع.
Until she sees pure whiteness. It is said: it is something like mucus that comes out at the end of menstruation. And it is said: it is the cotton with which a woman tests herself; if it comes out white, she has become pure. And menstruation drops the prayer from the menstruating woman. In it is an indication that prayer was obligatory upon her, then dropped. And the scholars of usul differed on this issue: whether rulings are established upon the minor, the insane, and the menstruating woman or not? Abu Zayd al-Dabusi chose that they are established, and the dropping is due to the excuse of hardship, saying: because the human being is the origin for the obligation of rights upon him; do you not see that he owes the tithe of his land and its kharaj by consensus?
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the termination of menstruation and its effect on prayer. The matn 'حتى ترى البياض الخالص' sets the criterion for purity: the woman is not pure until she sees clear white discharge. Two explanations are given: some say it is a mucus-like substance; others say it is determined by a cotton test—if the cotton comes out clean and white, she is pure. Then the second ruling: menstruation removes the obligation of prayer. The commentator notes that this implies prayer was originally obligatory upon her but is suspended during hayd. A brief usuli discussion follows: Abu Zayd al-Dabusi (a Hanafi usuli scholar) argues that rulings of obligation are established upon every human being in principle, including minors, the insane, and menstruating women, but the obligation is dropped due to hardship (حرج), not because they are not addressed. He supports this with the example of land tax (ushr and kharaj) being owed by everyone, including these categories, by consensus.

Key Terms
البياض الخالص (al-bayad al-khalis): Pure white discharge indicating the end of menstruation; often identified by a cotton test.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that serves as the excuse for dropping the obligation of prayer during menstruation, per Abu Zayd al-Dabusi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When she sees pure white discharge.
C) After a fixed number of days.
D) When she bathes (ghusl).

Key Takeaway
A woman is not pure from hayd until she sees pure white discharge; the prayer obligation is lifted due to hardship, not because it was never obligatory.

End of Menstruation and the Dispute on Discharge Order
Defines end of hayd and intra-Hanafi dispute on discharge order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the criterion for the end of hayd according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the order of kudrah and safa' discharge.

Core Idea
Menstruation ends with pure whiteness; dark discharge at the end indicates hayd throughout, even if order reverses due to anatomy.

This passage from the Jawharah al-Nayirah defines when menstruation ends and addresses a subtle difference among Hanafi imams about whether the sequence of discharge matters. Understanding this clarifies how a woman determines her state of purity for worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining sign of the end of hayd
Locate the phrase in the matn that states when menstruation ends. Note the term 'al-bayad al-khalis' (pure whiteness).
This is the agreed-upon criterion in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the general rule stated by 'the two'
The two scholars (likely Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) state that if the last day of the period is hayd, then the first day was also hayd. All days of hayd share one ruling.
This is based on qiyas: all menstrual blood is the same in legal effect.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection and its rebuttal
Abu Yusuf argues that dark discharge (kudrah) typically comes after clear discharge (safa'). The text rebuts by noting that the exit is from below due to the inverted womb, so kudrah exits first, like a jar punctured at the bottom.
The rebuttal uses an anatomical analogy to affirm that kudrah before safa' is still hayd.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Yusuf, if kudrah appears after safa', it would not be considered hayd. According to the majority, it is hayd regardless of order. The relied-upon view is the majority position.
This affects a woman's calculation of her menstrual days and purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحيض
حتى ترى البياض الخالص .
وهما يقولان ما كان حيضاً في آخر أيامها: كان حيضاً في أول أيامها، كالحمرة؛ لأن جميع مدة الحيض في حكم واحد.
وما قاله أبو يوسف إن خروج الكدرة يتأخر عن الصافي: إنما هو فيما إذا كان مخرجه من أعلاه، أما إذا كان من أسفله: فالكدرة تخرج قبل الصافي، وهنا المخرج من أسفل ؛ لأن فم الرحم منكوس، فتخرج الكدرة أولاً، كالجَرَّة إذا ثُقب أسفلها.
قوله : (حتى ترى البياض الخالص).
قيل : هو شيء يُشبه المخاط يخرج عند انتهاء الحيض. وقيل: هو القطن الذي تختبر به المرأةُ نفسها، إذا خرج أبيض: فقد
Chapter of Menstruation. Until she sees pure whiteness. And they two say: whatever was menstruation in her last days was menstruation in her first days, like redness, because all the duration of menstruation is in one ruling. And what Abu Yusuf said that the exit of dark discharge is delayed after clear [discharge] is only when its exit is from its top. As for when it is from its bottom, the dark discharge exits before the clear, and here the exit is from below because the mouth of the womb is inverted, so the dark discharge exits first, like a jar if its bottom is punctured. His saying: (Until she sees pure whiteness). It is said: it is a thing resembling mucus that comes out at the end of menstruation. And it is said: it is the cotton with which the woman tests herself, if it comes out white, then she has become pure.

Commentary
This passage defines the end of menstruation and discusses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the sequence of discharges. The matn states that hayd ends upon seeing pure whiteness (bayad khalis). The commentary expands with two interpretations: it is likened to mucus or to the white test cotton. The text then addresses a dispute: the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, or possibly Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?) hold that whatever was considered hayd at the end must have been hayd at the beginning too, analogous to redness. Abu Yusuf differs, claiming that dark discharge (kudrah) typically comes after clear discharge, but only if the exit is from the top. Since the mouth of the womb is anatomically inverted, the dark discharge actually exits first, as in a jar punctured at its base. The passage uses qiyas (analogical reasoning) to support the position that kudrah at the end can indicate hayd. The relied-upon view is that the end of hayd is determined by pure whiteness, and the order of discharges must be considered in light of anatomical reality.

Key Terms
البياض الخالص (al-bayāḍ al-khāliṣ): Pure whiteness; the sign that menstruation has ended.
الكدرة (al-kudrah): Turbid or dark discharge; a type of blood that can be part of menstruation.
فم الرحم منكوس (fam al-rahim mankūs): The mouth of the womb is inverted; a physical description used to explain the order of discharge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definitive sign that menstruation has ended?
A) The appearance of any discharge
B) Seeing pure white discharge (al-bayad al-khalis)
C) The absence of blood for three days
D) The passing of ten days

Key Takeaway
Menstruation ends with pure whiteness; dark discharge at the end remains menstruation regardless of order, based on the anatomical reality of the inverted womb.

Rulings on Fasting and Mosque for the Menstruating Woman
Explains prohibitions and makeup rules for fasting and prayer, and mosque entry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings for a menstruating woman regarding fasting, prayer, and mosque entry, and explain the reasoning behind the difference in makeup.

Core Idea
Fasting is forbidden but must be made up; prayer is dropped and not made up due to excessive burden.

In this passage, the author explains why different terminology is used for fasting and prayer during menstruation, and why fasting must be made up but prayer is not. The wisdom behind these rules reflects the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). You will learn the precise rulings and their underlying logic, which is essential for correctly applying these rules in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the Arabic carefully and list the three distinct rulings mentioned: fasting, prayer, and mosque entry. Note the precise terms used for each.
The rulings are: (1) fasting is forbidden, (2) prayer obligation is dropped, (3) mosque entry is forbidden.
2
Analyze the terminology: yuharrim vs yusqit
Understand why the author says 'yuharrim' (forbids) for fasting but 'yusqit' (drops) for prayer. Consider that fasting must be made up, so it is actively prohibited, while prayer is not made up, so its obligation is simply removed.
The term 'yuharrim' emphasizes the prohibition, while 'yusqit' indicates the obligation is lifted.
3
Understand the reasoning for makeup
Read the explanation: making up many prayers (fifty per month) would be burdensome, while fasting is only once a year. This demonstrates the principle of removing hardship from the ummah.
The burden of making up prayers is greater, so it is waived entirely.
4
Note the mosque prohibition
The third ruling is that she must not enter the mosque. This is based on the hadith and is a straightforward prohibition.
No makeup applies here; it is a pure prohibition.

His saying: (And fasting is forbidden for her). He said 'forbidden' in fasting, while for prayer he said 'drops', because making up fasting is obligatory, so mentioning dropping is not appropriate for it, and prayer is not made up, so mentioning dropping is suitable. His saying: (And she makes up fasting, and she does not make up prayer) because making up prayer involves hardship: in every day and night there are five prayers, so during the menstruation period there are fifty prayers, and this is every month. As for fasting, it occurs only once a year, so making it up does not cause her hardship. His saying: (And she does not enter the mosque). (1) Mughni al-Muhtaj 1/409. Commentary
This passage presents three distinct rulings for the menstruating woman. First, fasting is forbidden (tuharrim) rather than dropped (yusqit) because fasting must be made up later, making the term 'drop' inappropriate. Second, she must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers, because the burden of making up so many prayers would be excessive (fifty per month). Third, she is forbidden from entering a mosque. The commentary explains the reasoning behind these rulings. The marginal note mentions that according to al-Shafi'i, she must pay zakat (though this is not the Hanafi position), and a cross-reference to Mughni al-Muhtaj. These rulings are clear and easy to memorize.

Key Terms
يحرم (yuḥarrim): Forbidden; used for fasting during menstruation.
تقضي (taqḍī): She makes up; refers to obligatory fasts missed due to hayd.

Prohibitions During Menstruation in Hanafi Fiqh
Lists prohibited acts during menstruation with proofs and comments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five prohibitions for a menstruating woman in Hanafi fiqh and explain the rationale for each, particularly the distinction that she makes up missed fasts but not prayers.

Core Idea
Major acts of worship are prohibited during menstruation; only fasts are later made up, prayers are dropped due to hardship.

Menstruation (hayd) is a natural condition that triggers specific legal rulings. The Hanafi school, like others, prohibits several acts of worship and marital relations during this time, but its rationale for why prayers are not made up (while fasts are) reflects a principle of avoiding excessive hardship. In this lesson, we examine the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri that details each prohibition and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five prohibitions
Read the passage carefully and list all acts that are prohibited for a menstruating woman. The text explicitly mentions fasting, prayer (not made up), entering the mosque, tawaf, and marital relations.
Note that the prohibition of entering the mosque includes the roof of the mosque.
2
Understand the distinction in qada (making up)
The passage explains that fasting is prohibited but must be made up later, while prayer is completely dropped and not made up. The reason given is the hardship of making up numerous prayers each month.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh and based on the principle of mashaqqa (hardship).
3
Examine the ruling on entering the mosque
The text prohibits entering the mosque and extends this to the roof of the mosque, treating it as part of the mosque structure. The same ruling applies to a junub (person in major impurity).
This extension is based on the legal principle that the roof is considered part of the mosque (sath al-masjid).
4
Analyze the ruling on tawaf
Although tawaf requires entering the mosque, the prohibition is mentioned separately to cover cases where menstruation begins after entering the mosque and to remove the misconception that tawaf is allowed because other Hajj rites (like standing at Arafat) are permitted.
This shows the commentator's thoroughness in addressing potential misunderstandings.
5
Review the marital relations prohibition and consequences
The husband is prohibited from sexual relations during menstruation, based on Quran 2:222. The passage outlines severe consequences: if done considering it lawful, it is kufr; if not, repentance and charity are recommended.
The use of euphemism (kinaayah) follows Quranic style.

Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, listing the prohibitions and obligations for a woman in menstruation (hayd). The author, a Hanafi scholar, explains the reasoning behind each ruling.

First, fasting is prohibited for the menstruating woman. The commentator notes that the matn uses 'prohibits' for fasting because making up fasts later is obligatory, so 'dropping' is not appropriate. For prayer, the matn says 'she does not make up prayers'—the commentator says prayer is completely dropped due to the hardship of making up so many prayers each month, whereas fasting only occurs once a year. This distinction is based on ease and hardship (mashaqqa).

Second, she must make up the missed fasts but not the prayers.

Third, she is not permitted to enter the mosque. This applies to the masjid building, including its roof (sath al-masjid) because it is considered part of the mosque. The same rule applies to a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub).

Fourth, she may not circumambulate (tawaf) the Kaaba. Even though tawaf requires entering the mosque, this ruling is explicitly mentioned to cover the case where her menses begins after she has entered the mosque and started tawaf. It also removes the misconception that since she can perform other Hajj rites like standing at Arafat, she might think tawaf is also permissible.

Fifth, her husband may not have sexual relations with her during menstruation. The commentator uses euphemism (kinaayah) following the Quran. The prohibition is severe: if the husband deliberately violates it considering the act lawful, he commits disbelief (kufr). If he does so without considering it lawful, he must repent and seek forgiveness, and it is recommended to give charity of one dinar or half a dinar.

The passage also briefly mentions a disagreement about zakat (not fully elaborated here) referencing al-Shafi'i and al-Bazdawi, but the focus is clearly on the rulings for the menstruating woman.

Key Terms
حائض (ha'id): A woman experiencing menstruation (hayd), to whom specific prohibitions apply.
قضاء (qada): Making up missed obligatory acts of worship, such as fasting, after the excuse (menstruation) ends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fasting
B) Prayer
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman is prohibited from praying, fasting, entering the mosque, performing tawaf, and marital relations; she must make up fasts but not prayers.

Prohibitions During Menstruation: Tawaf and Marital Relations
States prohibitions for menstruating woman and junub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two prohibitions for a menstruating woman, explain the reason for mentioning tawaf separately, and describe the ruling on intercourse including the recommended expiation.

Core Idea
Intercourse with a menstruating wife is haram; expiation is recommended charity.

The chapter on menstruation begins with clear prohibitions: the menstruating woman must not perform tawaf, and her husband must not have intercourse with her. These rulings are foundational to understanding the state of ha'id in Hanafi fiqh. The author also clarifies why tawaf is mentioned separately even though it requires entering the mosque, which is already prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibitions
Read the opening sentences: 'she should not perform tawaf' and 'her husband should not come to her.' Note that both apply to the menstruating woman and the junub.
The roof of the mosque shares the same ruling as the mosque itself.
2
Analyze the reason for mentioning tawaf
The commentator addresses a potential objection: since tawaf requires entering the mosque (already prohibited), why mention tawaf? Two scenarios are given: (1) if menstruation begins after she has entered the mosque and started tawaf, and (2) to remove the misconception that tawaf is permitted because other Hajj rites like standing at Arafat are permitted.
This shows the thoroughness of Hanafi fiqh in anticipating questions.
3
Understand the ruling on intercourse
Intercourse is strictly haram. If done considering it lawful, it is apostasy. If done without considering it lawful, repentance is required. Additionally, it is recommended to give charity: a dinar if at the beginning of the period, half a dinar if at the end or middle.
The charity is on the husband alone and disbursed like zakat.

Chapter of Menstruation. She should not perform tawaf around the House, nor should her husband come to her. And likewise the one in major ritual impurity (junub) also. The roof of the mosque has the same ruling as the mosque, such that it is not permissible for the menstruating woman and the junub to stand on it, because it is in its ruling. If it is said: Tawaf is only done by entering the mosque, and it is already known that both are prohibited from that, so what is the benefit in mentioning tawaf? It is said: That can be conceived when menstruation comes to her after she entered the mosque and had begun tawaf. Or it is said: Since the menstruating woman can do what the pilgrim does of standing (at 'Arafat), one might think that she is also permitted to perform tawaf, just as standing is permitted for her, and other things; one might think that, and it is stronger (i.e., tawaf is more likely to be thought permissible), so He removed this false impression by that. His statement: 'Nor should her husband come to her.' He mentioned it in the form of a euphemism; out of politeness, good character, and following the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then when they have purified themselves, go in unto them...' (al-Baqarah 2:222). And if he has intercourse with her considering it lawful, he becomes an apostate; and if he does so without considering it lawful, repentance and seeking forgiveness are incumbent upon him. And it is said: It is recommended that he give in charity a dinar, and it is said: half a dinar. Reconciliation between them: if it is at the beginning (of her period): a dinar; and if at the end or middle: half a dinar. Is that upon the man alone or upon both of them? The apparent (position) is that it is upon him, not her. And its disbursement is the same as that of zakat. And it is permissible for him to kiss her, lie with her, and enjoy her entire body except between the navel and the knee according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: He enjoys her entire body, but avoids the 'sha'ar' (area) of blood, no more, and that is the place of its exit. It is not permissible for her to conceal menstruation from her husband in order for him to have intercourse with her without his knowledge. Likewise, it is not permissible for her to claim that she is menstruating when she is not, in order to prevent him from having intercourse with her; because of the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Allah has cursed the gha'isah (one who conceals) and the maghusah (one who fakes).' So the gha'isah is the one who does not inform her husband that she is menstruating, so he has intercourse with her without knowledge. (1) [Footnote: Gharib al-Hadith by al-Khattabi, 3/202, and he did not mention a chain for it; it was transmitted by the authors of Gharib works, like Ibn al-Athir in al-Nihayah, 3/395, and others; it has a supporting witness in meaning, but with a remote wording, namely: 'Allah has cursed the musawwifah and the mufassilah.' He said about it in Majma' al-Zawa'id 4/296: narrated by Abu Ya'la, and in its chain is Yahya ibn al-'Ala', who is weak and abandoned. Then he mentioned another witness also weak. See Fayd al-Qadir by al-Munawi, 5/292.]

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nirah is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, beginning the chapter on menstruation. The author first states two key prohibitions for the menstruating woman: she must not perform tawaf (circumambulation of the Ka'bah) and her husband must not have intercourse with her. The same prohibitions apply to the one in major ritual impurity (junub). The roof of the mosque shares the ruling of the mosque itself, so both the menstruating woman and the junub are prohibited from standing on it because it is considered part of the mosque. The commentator then explains why the prohibition of tawaf is mentioned separately, although it already implies entry into the mosque: there are two scenarios where this is useful. First, if menstruation begins after she has already entered the mosque and started tawaf, the prohibition becomes relevant. Second, lest one mistakenly think that since the menstruating woman is permitted to stand at 'Arafat (which is an intense rite of Hajj), she might also be permitted to perform tawaf, which is less intense — the text removes this misconception. Next, the prohibition of intercourse is stated euphemistically, following the Quranic style, to teach politeness. If a man has intercourse with his menstruating wife while considering it lawful (i.e., rejecting the prohibition), he becomes an apostate (kafir). If he does so without considering it lawful, he must repent and seek forgiveness. Additionally, it is recommended (mustahabb) to give charity: a full dinar if the intercourse occurred at the beginning of her period, and half a dinar if at the end or middle. This charity is on the husband alone, not the wife, and it is given to the recipients of zakat. The passage then discusses permissible intimacy. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the husband may kiss, lie in bed, and enjoy his wife's entire body except between the navel and the knee. Imam Muhammad, however, has a more permissive view: he may enjoy her entire body except the exact area of blood flow (i.e., the vagina). Finally, the wife is prohibited from two forms of deception: (1) concealing her menstruation to allow intercourse without her husband's knowledge, and (2) falsely claiming menstruation to prevent intercourse. Both are condemned by the hadith, which curses the 'gha'isah' (one who conceals) and 'maghusah' (one who fakes). The hadith is narrated with weak chains but is accepted in meaning.

Key Terms
حائض (ḥāʾiḍ): A woman experiencing menstruation (hayḍ) during which certain acts of worship and marital relations are prohibited.
مستحل (mustaḥill): One who considers a prohibited act lawful, thereby rejecting the prohibition and committing apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man has intercourse with his menstruating wife without considering it lawful, what is the recommended action?
A) He must offer a kaffarah of fasting two months.
B) He must give a dinar or half a dinar in charity, repent, and seek forgiveness.
C) He must divorce her.
D) He must perform a hadd punishment.

Key Takeaway
The menstruating woman is prohibited from tawaf and marital intercourse; violating the intercourse prohibition requires repentance and recommended charity.

Permissible Intimacy During Menstruation: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on extent of permissible intimacy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on permissible intimacy during menstruation, identify the relied-upon view, and explain the practical difference between them.

Core Idea
Husband may enjoy wife's body during menstruation except between navel and knee (relied-upon view) or except the vagina alone (Muhammad's view).

While intercourse is absolutely prohibited during menstruation, the question of what other forms of intimacy are permitted arises. The Hanafi school has an intra-school dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two famous students of Abu Hanifa) and Imam Muhammad himself regarding the permissible area of enjoyment. This lesson examines the positions and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground
Both positions agree that kissing, lying in bed, and general enjoyment are permissible. The dispute is only about the area of the body that must be avoided.
2
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn)
According to them, the husband may enjoy the entire body except the area between the navel and the knee.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad alone
Imam Muhammad says the husband may enjoy the entire body except the exact area where blood exits (the vagina).
This is a more permissive view.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference lies in whether touching the thighs and lower belly is permitted. According to the Sahibayn, it is not; according to Imam Muhammad, it is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحيض ولا تطوف بالبيت، ولا يأتيها زوجها . وكذا الجنب أيضاً. وسطح المسجد : له حكم المسجد، حتى لا يَحِلُّ للحائض والجنب الوقوف عليه؛ لأنه في حكمه. قوله: (ولا تطوف بالبيت). فإن قيل: الطواف لا يكون إلا بدخول المسجد، وقد عُرف منعهما منه، فما الفائدة في ذكر الطواف؟ قيل : يُتصور ذلك فيما إذا جاءها الحيض بعد ما دخلت المسجد، وقد شرعت في الطواف. أو يقال: لما كان للحائض أن تصنع ما يصنعه الحاج من الوقوف ظان أنه يجوز لها الطواف أيضاً، كما جاز لها الوقوف، وغيره، ربما يظن وهو أقوى منه، فأزال هذا الوهم بذلك. قوله: (ولا يأتيها زوجها). ذكره بلفظ الكناية؛ تأدباً وتخلقاً واقتداء بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا تَطَهَّرْنَ فَأْتُوهُ ... البقرة / ٢٢٢ . وإن أتاها مُستَحلاً كَفَرَ ، وإن أتاها غير مستحل فعليه التوبة والاستغفار. وقيل : يُستحب أن يتصدق بدينار، وقيل: بنصف دينار، والتوفيق بينهما : إن كان في أوله : فدينار، وإن كان في آخره، أو وسطه: فنصف دينار. وهل ذلك على الرجل وحده، أو عليهما جميعاً؟ الظاهر أنه عليه، دونها. ومصرفه : مصرف الزكاة. وله أن يُقبلها، ويضاجعها، ويستمتع بجميع بدنها ما خلا ما بين السرة والركبة عندهما، وقال محمد : يستمتع بجميع بدنها، ويجتنب شعار الدم، لا غير، وهو موضع خروجه. ولا يحل لها أن تكتم الحيض على زوجها ؛ ليجامعها بغير علم منه. وكذا لا يحل لها أن تُظهر أنها حائض من غير حيض؛ لتمنعه مجامعتها؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لعن الله الغائصة والمغوصة»(١). فالغائصة التي لا تُعلم زوجها أنها حائض، فيجامعها بغير علم. (١) غريب الحديث للخطابي ،۲۰۲/۳، ولم يذكر له سنداً، ونقله عنه أصحاب الغريب، كصاحب النهاية لابن الأثير ،٣٩٥/٣ ، وغيره، وله شاهد بمعناه، لكن بلفظ بعيد، وهو: «لعن الله المسوفة، والمُفَسلة»، قال عنه في مجمع الزوائد ٢٩٦/٤: رواه أبو يعلى، وفيه: يحيى بن العلاء، وهو ضعيف متروك. اهـ، ثم ذكر له شاهداً آخر، وفيه ضعف أيضاً، وينظر فيض القدير للمناوي ٢٩٢/٥.
Chapter of Menstruation. She should not perform tawaf around the House, nor should her husband come to her. And likewise the one in major ritual impurity (junub) also. The roof of the mosque has the same ruling as the mosque, such that it is not permissible for the menstruating woman and the junub to stand on it, because it is in its ruling. His statement: 'She should not perform tawaf around the House.' If it is said: Tawaf is only done by entering the mosque, and it is already known that both are prohibited from that, so what is the benefit in mentioning tawaf? It is said: That can be conceived when menstruation comes to her after she entered the mosque and had begun tawaf. Or it is said: Since the menstruating woman can do what the pilgrim does of standing (at 'Arafat), one might think that she is also permitted to perform tawaf, just as standing is permitted for her, and other things; one might think that, and it is stronger (i.e., tawaf is more likely to be thought permissible), so He removed this false impression by that. His statement: 'Nor should her husband come to her.' He mentioned it in the form of a euphemism; out of politeness, good character, and following the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then when they have purified themselves, go in unto them...' (al-Baqarah 2:222). And if he has intercourse with her considering it lawful, he becomes an apostate; and if he does so without considering it lawful, repentance and seeking forgiveness are incumbent upon him. And it is said: It is recommended that he give in charity a dinar, and it is said: half a dinar. Reconciliation between them: if it is at the beginning (of her period): a dinar; and if at the end or middle: half a dinar. Is that upon the man alone or upon both of them? The apparent (position) is that it is upon him, not her. And its disbursement is the same as that of zakat. And it is permissible for him to kiss her, lie with her, and enjoy her entire body except between the navel and the knee according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: He enjoys her entire body, but avoids the 'sha'ar' (area) of blood, no more, and that is the place of its exit. It is not permissible for her to conceal menstruation from her husband in order for him to have intercourse with her without his knowledge. Likewise, it is not permissible for her to claim that she is menstruating when she is not, in order to prevent him from having intercourse with her; because of the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Allah has cursed the gha'isah (one who conceals) and the maghusah (one who fakes).' So the gha'isah is the one who does not inform her husband that she is menstruating, so he has intercourse with her without knowledge. (1) [Footnote: Gharib al-Hadith by al-Khattabi, 3/202, and he did not mention a chain for it; it was transmitted by the authors of Gharib works, like Ibn al-Athir in al-Nihayah, 3/395, and others; it has a supporting witness in meaning, but with a remote wording, namely: 'Allah has cursed the musawwifah and the mufassilah.' He said about it in Majma' al-Zawa'id 4/296: narrated by Abu Ya'la, and in its chain is Yahya ibn al-'Ala', who is weak and abandoned. Then he mentioned another witness also weak. See Fayd al-Qadir by al-Munawi, 5/292.]
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nirah is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, beginning the chapter on menstruation. The author first states two key prohibitions for the menstruating woman: she must not perform tawaf (circumambulation of the Ka'bah) and her husband must not have intercourse with her. The same prohibitions apply to the one in major ritual impurity (junub). The roof of the mosque shares the ruling of the mosque itself, so both the menstruating woman and the junub are prohibited from standing on it because it is considered part of the mosque. The commentator then explains why the prohibition of tawaf is mentioned separately, although it already implies entry into the mosque: there are two scenarios where this is useful. First, if menstruation begins after she has already entered the mosque and started tawaf, the prohibition becomes relevant. Second, lest one mistakenly think that since the menstruating woman is permitted to stand at 'Arafat (which is an intense rite of Hajj), she might also be permitted to perform tawaf, which is less intense — the text removes this misconception. Next, the prohibition of intercourse is stated euphemistically, following the Quranic style, to teach politeness. If a man has intercourse with his menstruating wife while considering it lawful (i.e., rejecting the prohibition), he becomes an apostate (kafir). If he does so without considering it lawful, he must repent and seek forgiveness. Additionally, it is recommended (mustahabb) to give charity: a full dinar if the intercourse occurred at the beginning of her period, and half a dinar if at the end or middle. This charity is on the husband alone, not the wife, and it is given to the recipients of zakat. The passage then discusses permissible intimacy. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the husband may kiss, lie in bed, and enjoy his wife's entire body except between the navel and the knee. Imam Muhammad, however, has a more permissive view: he may enjoy her entire body except the exact area of blood flow (i.e., the vagina). Finally, the wife is prohibited from two forms of deception: (1) concealing her menstruation to allow intercourse without her husband's knowledge, and (2) falsely claiming menstruation to prevent intercourse. Both are condemned by the hadith, which curses the 'gha'isah' (one who conceals) and 'maghusah' (one who fakes). The hadith is narrated with weak chains but is accepted in meaning.

Key Terms
عندهما (ʿindahumā): According to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
شعار الدم (shiʿār al-dam): The area of blood flow, i.e., the vagina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, which area of the wife's body is prohibited for the husband to enjoy during her menstruation?
A) The entire body except the vagina.
B) The area between the navel and the knee.
C) The area between the chest and the knees.
D) The entire body is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits considerable intimacy during menstruation, with the relied-upon view prohibiting only the area between navel and knee.

Prohibition of Deception Regarding Menstruation: The Cursed Acts
Prohibition of deception about menstruation with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define gha'isah and maghusah, explain the prohibition of both acts, and evaluate the strength of the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Concealing menstruation to lure husband into intercourse or faking it to repel him are both haram and cursed.

The passage concludes with a strong warning against deception regarding menstruation. Two types of deceit are condemned: concealing menstruation to allow intercourse, and falsely claiming menstruation to prevent it. The Prophet (peace be upon him) cursed both categories. This lesson examines the ruling and the hadith evidence, which is weak but supported by meaning.

Guided Path
1
Define the two terms
Gha'isah is the woman who conceals her menstruation so her husband has intercourse without knowledge. Maghusah is the woman who falsely claims menstruation to avoid intercourse.
The terminology is derived from the hadith.
2
State the prohibition
Both acts are haram. The hadith explicitly curses them, indicating the severity.
The curse indicates the act is a major sin (kabirah).
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith is reported with a weak chain, but the meaning is supported by other narrations and by the general prohibition of deceit in Islam.
The text notes the weakness but includes it because the ruling is intrinsically sound.

Compensation for Intercourse During Menstruation (Kaffara)
Ruling on compensation for intercourse during menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the amount of kaffara for intercourse during menstruation and identify who is liable to pay it.

Core Idea
The kaffara for intercourse during menstruation varies by timing and is the husband's sole responsibility.

When a husband has intercourse with his menstruating wife, Islamic law prescribes a financial compensation (kaffara). This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the amount and liability derived from the commentaries of Al-Quduri and Al-Marghinani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
The act in question is sexual intercourse with a menstruating wife, which is prohibited. The text discusses the required expiation.
2
Determine the Timing
The kaffara depends on when the intercourse occurs: at the beginning of the period (one dinar) or at the end or middle (half a dinar).
The beginning is the first days when blood is fresh and heavy.
3
Assess Liability
The kaffara is upon the husband alone, not the wife, and it is disbursed like zakat.
This implies it is a financial penalty for his transgression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحيض
بينهما : إن كان في أوله : فدينار، وإن كان في آخره، أو وسطه: فنصف دينار.
- وهل ذلك على الرجل وحده، أو عليهما جميعاً؟
الظاهر أنه عليه، دونها.
- ومصرفه : مصرف الزكاة.
وله أن يُقبلها، ويضاجعها، ويستمتع بجميع بدنها ما خلا ما بين السرة والركبة عندهما، وقال محمد : يستمتع بجميع بدنها، ويجتنب شعار الدم، لا غير، وهو موضع خروجه.
ولا يحل لها أن تكتم الحيض على زوجها ؛ ليجامعها بغير علم منه. وكذا لا يحل لها أن تُظهر أنها حائض من غير حيض؛ لتمنعه مجامعتها؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لعن الله الغائصة والمغوصة»(۱). فالغائصة التي لا تُعلم زوجها أنها حائض، فيجامعها بغير علم.
(۱) غريب الحديث للخطابي ،۲۰۲/۳، ولم يذكر له سنداً، ونقله عنه أصحاب الغريب، كصاحب النهاية لابن الأثير ،٣٩٥/٣ ، وغيره، وله شاهد بمعناه، لكن بلفظ بعيد، وهو: «لعن الله المسوفة، والمُفَسلة»، قال عنه في مجمع الزوائد ٢٩٦/٤: رواه أبو يعلى، وفيه: يحيى بن العلاء، وهو ضعيف متروك. اهـ، ثم ذكر له شاهداً آخر، وفيه ضعف أيضاً، وينظر فيض القدير للمناوي ٢٩٢/٥.

باب الحيض
ولا يجوز لحائض، ولا جُنُب قراءة القرآن .
والمغوصةُ: التي تقول لزوجها : إنها حائض، وهي طاهرة؛ حتى لا يجامعها.
وأما الوطء في الدبر : فحرام في حالة الحيض والطهر؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَأْتُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَمَرَكُمُ اللَّهُ . البقرة / ۲۲۲، أي من حيث أمركم الله بتجنبه في الحيض، وهو الفرج.
وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: إتيان النساء في أعجاز هنَّ حرام (۱).
وقال: «ملعون من أتى امرأة في دبرها (٢).
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأْتُوا حَرْثَكُمْ أَنَّى شِنْتُمْ. البقرة/٢٢٣: أي كيف شئتم ومتى شئتم ،مقبلات ومدبرات ومستقلبات، وباركات، بعد أن يكون في الفرج.
ولأن الله تعالى سمى الزوجة حرثاً، فإنها للولد، كالأرض للزرع، وهذا دليل على تحريم الوطء في الدبر ؛ لأنه موضع الفرث، لا موضع الحرث.
قوله: (ولا يجوز لحائض ولا جُنُب قراءة القرآن).
(۱) بلفظ : «إتيان النساء في محاشهن حرام في الآثار لأبي يوسف ص١٣٤ (٦١٥)، وبلفظ: «إتيان النساء في أدبارهن حرام في سنن النسائي الكبرى (٨٩٤٦)
(٢) سنن أبي داود (٢١٦٢)، مسند أحمد ۲۷۲/۲، وله طرق وشواهد عديدة يعضد بعضها بعضاً، ينظر لها البدر المنير ۲۹۹/۱۹ ، التلخيص الحبير ١٨٠/٣.
Chapter of Menstruation
Between them: If it was at its beginning, then one dinar; and if at its end or middle, then half a dinar.
- And is that upon the man alone, or upon both of them?
The apparent is that it is upon him, not her.
- And its disbursement is the disbursement of zakat.
And it is permissible for him to kiss her, and to lie with her, and to enjoy all of her body except what is between the navel and the knee according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: He enjoys all of her body, and avoids the trace of blood, nothing else, and it is the place of its exit.
And it is not permissible for her to conceal menstruation from her husband so that he has intercourse with her without his knowledge. Likewise, it is not permissible for her to show that she is menstruating when she is not, to prevent him from having intercourse with her; due to his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'May Allah curse the ghā'iṣah and the maghūṣah.' (1) For the ghā'iṣah is the one who does not inform her husband that she is menstruating, so he has intercourse with her without knowledge.
(1) [Hadith source footnote] ...

Chapter of Menstruation
And it is not permissible for a menstruating woman nor for a person in major ritual impurity to recite the Quran.
And the maghūṣah is the one who tells her husband that she is menstruating while she is pure, so that he does not have intercourse with her.
As for anal intercourse, it is forbidden during menstruation and purity; due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'So come to them from where Allah has commanded you' (Al-Baqarah 2:222), meaning from where Allah has commanded you to avoid during menstruation, which is the vulva.
And he said, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Intercourse with women in their anuses is forbidden.' (1)
And he said: 'Cursed is he who has intercourse with a woman in her anus.' (2)
And as for the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Your wives are a tilth to you, so come to your tilth however you wish' (Al-Baqarah 2:223): meaning however you wish and whenever you wish, face to face or from behind, standing or kneeling, as long as it is in the vulva.
And because Allah Almighty called the wife a tilth, for she is for offspring, like the earth for cultivation, and this is evidence for the prohibition of anal intercourse; because it is the place of feces, not the place of cultivation.
His saying: (And it is not permissible for a menstruating woman nor for a person in major ritual impurity to recite the Quran).
(1) With the wording: 'Intercourse with women in their anuses is forbidden' in Al-Athar of Abu Yusuf p.134 (615), and with wording: 'Intercourse with women in their anuses is forbidden' in Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra (8946)
(2) Sunan Abi Dawud (2162), Musnad Ahmad 2/272, and it has many chains and supporting evidences that strengthen each other, see al-Badr al-Munir 19/299, al-Talkhis al-Habir 3/180.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, presents several rulings related to menstruation. The text begins by discussing the compensation (kaffara) due for intercourse during menstruation: one dinar if at the beginning, half a dinar if at the end or middle. This is a ruling the author attributes to Abu Hanifa and his companions, with the opinion that it is on the husband alone, not the wife, and the amount is disbursed like zakat.

Next, the text addresses permissible physical contact with a menstruating woman. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), a husband may kiss, lie with her, and enjoy all of her body except the area between the navel and knees. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, reports a different view (apparently his own or a transmission) that the husband may enjoy all of her body while avoiding only the actual blood site. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.

The text then forbids a wife from concealing her menstruation to trick her husband into intercourse, and also forbids falsely claiming menstruation to avoid intercourse. This is supported by a hadith (albeit with weak chains) cursing the 'ghā'iṣah' (one who hides menstruation) and 'maghūṣah' (one who falsely claims it). The commentary explains the terms.

On page 238, the text states that a menstruating woman and a person in major ritual impurity (junub) may not recite the Quran. This is a prohibition, typically understood in the Hanafi school as makruh tahrimi (close to haram) for the menstruating woman, but the text simply says 'la yajuz' (not permissible).

Finally, the passage discusses anal intercourse, declaring it haram under all circumstances, whether during menstruation or purity. The proof is from Quran (2:222) which commands 'come to them from where Allah has commanded you,' interpreted as the vulva, and from hadith explicitly forbidding anal intercourse. The author also argues from the analogy: a wife is called 'tilth' (for offspring), so the proper place is the vagina, not the anus which is for waste.

Key Terms
دينار (dinar): A gold coin; here it is a unit of compensation equivalent to approximately 4.25 grams of gold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is liable to pay the kaffara for intercourse during menstruation?
A) The wife
B) The husband
C) Both equally
D) No one; it is not required

Key Takeaway
The kaffara for intercourse during menstruation is wajib on the husband alone, varying by timing, and is distributed like zakat.

Permissible Physical Contact with a Menstruating Wife
Intra-Hanafi dispute on physical intimacy during menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on permissible physical contact with a menstruating wife and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The Hanafi majority permits all contact except between navel and knee; a minority restricts only the blood site.

While intercourse is clearly prohibited during menstruation, the question of other physical intimacy arises. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on what parts of the wife's body may be enjoyed.

Guided Path
1
Note the Default Permissibility
The text states it is permissible (lahu) for the husband to kiss, lie with, and enjoy his menstruating wife's body, establishing a baseline of allowance.
The prohibition is limited in scope.
2
State the Majority Position (Sahibayn)
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the husband may enjoy all of the body except the area between the navel and the knee.
This includes the thighs, abdomen, etc.
3
State the Alternate Position (Muhammad alone)
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani also reports a view that the husband may enjoy the entire body, avoiding only the actual site where blood exits (the vulva).
This is a more lenient view.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the view of the two companions (the majority), as it is more cautious and consistent with the spirit of avoiding the area of pollution.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, presents several rulings related to menstruation. The text begins by discussing the compensation (kaffara) due for intercourse during menstruation: one dinar if at the beginning, half a dinar if at the end or middle. This is a ruling the author attributes to Abu Hanifa and his companions, with the opinion that it is on the husband alone, not the wife, and the amount is disbursed like zakat.

Next, the text addresses permissible physical contact with a menstruating woman. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), a husband may kiss, lie with her, and enjoy all of her body except the area between the navel and knees. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, reports a different view (apparently his own or a transmission) that the husband may enjoy all of her body while avoiding only the actual blood site. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.

The text then forbids a wife from concealing her menstruation to trick her husband into intercourse, and also forbids falsely claiming menstruation to avoid intercourse. This is supported by a hadith (albeit with weak chains) cursing the 'ghā'iṣah' (one who hides menstruation) and 'maghūṣah' (one who falsely claims it). The commentary explains the terms.

On page 238, the text states that a menstruating woman and a person in major ritual impurity (junub) may not recite the Quran. This is a prohibition, typically understood in the Hanafi school as makruh tahrimi (close to haram) for the menstruating woman, but the text simply says 'la yajuz' (not permissible).

The author also argues from the analogy: a wife is called 'tilth' (for offspring), so the proper place is the vagina, not the anus which is for waste.

Key Terms
شعار الدم (shi'ār al-dam): The site of blood, i.e., the vulva and surrounding area where menstrual blood exits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits most physical intimacy with a menstruating wife, but the relied-upon view prohibits contact between navel and knee.

Prohibition of Deception Regarding Menstruation
Prohibition of deceit regarding menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ghā'iṣah and maghūṣah and state the Hanafi ruling on concealing or falsely claiming menstruation.

Core Idea
Both concealing and falsely claiming menstruation to deceive one's husband are major sins (haram).

Deception in matters of menstruation undermines trust and the legal framework of family life. This lesson explains the two forbidden acts: hiding menstruation to allow intercourse, and pretending to menstruate to prevent it, supported by a hadith cursing such women.

Guided Path
1
Define the Two Forbidden Acts
Identify ghā'iṣah (one who hides menstruation so husband has intercourse unknowingly) and maghūṣah (one who falsely claims menstruation to avoid intercourse).
2
State the Ruling
Both acts are 'la yahillu' (not permissible), i.e., haram.
3
Analyze the Proof
The hadith 'L'an Allah al-ghā'iṣah wa al-maghūṣah' is cited. Although the chain is weak, the meaning is considered sound and supported by other evidence.
The curse indicates severe prohibition.
4
Note the Wisdom and Implications
These prohibitions protect the marital relationship from manipulation and uphold honesty.

(۱) بلفظ : «إتيان النساء في محاشهن حرام في الآثار لأبي يوسف ص١٣٤ (٦١٥)، وبلفظ: «إتيان النساء في أدبارهن حرام في سنن النسائي الكبرى (٨٩٤٦)
(٢) سنن أبي داود (٢١٦٢)، مسند أحمد ۲۷۲/۲، وله طرق وشواهد عديدة يعضد بعضها بعضاً، ينظر لها البدر المنير ۲۹۹/۱۹ ، التلخيص الحبير ١٨٠/٣.
Chapter of Menstruation
Between them: If it was at its beginning, then one dinar; and if at its end or middle, then half a dinar.
- And is that upon the man alone, or upon both of them?
The apparent is that it is upon him, not her.
- And its disbursement is the disbursement of zakat.
And it is permissible for him to kiss her, and to lie with her, and to enjoy all of her body except what is between the navel and the knee according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: He enjoys all of her body, and avoids the trace of blood, nothing else, and it is the place of its exit.
And it is not permissible for her to conceal menstruation from her husband so that he has intercourse with her without his knowledge. Likewise, it is not permissible for her to show that she is menstruating when she is not, to prevent him from having intercourse with her; due to his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'May Allah curse the ghā'iṣah and the maghūṣah.' Chapter of Menstruation
And it is not permissible for a menstruating woman nor for a person in major ritual impurity to recite the Quran.
And the maghūṣah is the one who tells her husband that she is menstruating while she is pure, so that he does not have intercourse with her.
As for anal intercourse, it is forbidden during menstruation and purity; due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'So come to them from where Allah has commanded you' (Al-Baqarah 2:222), meaning from where Allah has commanded you to avoid during menstruation, which is the vulva.
And he said, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Intercourse with women in their anuses is forbidden.' (1)
And he said: 'Cursed is he who has intercourse with a woman in her anus.' (2)
And as for the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Your wives are a tilth to you, so come to your tilth however you wish' (Al-Baqarah 2:223): meaning however you wish and whenever you wish, face to face or from behind, standing or kneeling, as long as it is in the vulva.
And because Allah Almighty called the wife a tilth, for she is for offspring, like the earth for cultivation, and this is evidence for the prohibition of anal intercourse; because it is the place of feces, not the place of cultivation.
His saying: (And it is not permissible for a menstruating woman nor for a person in major ritual impurity to recite the Quran).
(1) With the wording: 'Intercourse with women in their anuses is forbidden' in Al-Athar of Abu Yusuf p.134 (615), and with wording: 'Intercourse with women in their anuses is forbidden' in Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra (8946)
(2) Sunan Abi Dawud (2162), Musnad Ahmad 2/272, and it has many chains and supporting evidences that strengthen each other, see al-Badr al-Munir 19/299, al-Talkhis al-Habir 3/180.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, presents several rulings related to menstruation. The text begins by discussing the compensation (kaffara) due for intercourse during menstruation: one dinar if at the beginning, half a dinar if at the end or middle. This is a ruling the author attributes to Abu Hanifa and his companions, with the opinion that it is on the husband alone, not the wife, and the amount is disbursed like zakat.

Next, the text addresses permissible physical contact with a menstruating woman. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), a husband may kiss, lie with her, and enjoy all of her body except the area between the navel and knees. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, reports a different view (apparently his own or a transmission) that the husband may enjoy all of her body while avoiding only the actual blood site. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.

The text then forbids a wife from concealing her menstruation to trick her husband into intercourse, and also forbids falsely claiming menstruation to avoid intercourse. This is supported by a hadith (albeit with weak chains) cursing the 'ghā'iṣah' (one who hides menstruation) and 'maghūṣah' (one who falsely claims it). The commentary explains the terms.

On page 238, the text states that a menstruating woman and a person in major ritual impurity (junub) may not recite the Quran. This is a prohibition, typically understood in the Hanafi school as makruh tahrimi (close to haram) for the menstruating woman, but the text simply says 'la yajuz' (not permissible).

Finally, the passage discusses anal intercourse, declaring it haram under all circumstances, whether during menstruation or purity. The proof is from Quran (2:222) which commands 'come to them from where Allah has commanded you,' interpreted as the vulva, and from hadith explicitly forbidding anal intercourse. The author also argues from the analogy: a wife is called 'tilth' (for offspring), so the proper place is the vagina, not the anus which is for waste.

Key Terms
الغائصة (al-ghā'iṣah): A woman who hides her menstruation from her husband so that he has intercourse without knowing.
المغوصة (al-maghūṣah): A woman who falsely claims menstruation to prevent her husband from having intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a wife who tells her husband she is menstruating to avoid marital relations when she is actually pure?
A) Permissible if she is tired
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Permissible if she asks for divorce

Key Takeaway
Concealing or falsely claiming menstruation to deceive one's husband is a major sin (haram) in the Hanafi school.

Prohibition of Anal Intercourse
Prohibition of anal intercourse with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on anal intercourse and cite the primary proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and analogy.

Core Idea
Anal intercourse is haram in all states, whether during menstruation or purity, based on Quranic command, prophetic curses, and rational analogy.

The Hanafi school is unequivocal: anal intercourse is forbidden at all times. This lesson examines the textual and rational proofs presented in Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, including Quranic verses, hadith, and the analogy of the wife as 'tilth' (harth).

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Anal intercourse is 'حرام' (forbidden) during menstruation and even during purity (non-menstrual state).
The prohibition is absolute.
2
Examine the Quranic Proof
Verse 2:222 commands: 'So come to them from where Allah has commanded you.' The interpretation: the commanded place is the vulva, not the anus.
The phrase 'from where' indicates the proper place.
3
Examine the Hadith Proofs
Two hadith are cited: 'Intercourse with women in their anuses is forbidden' and 'Cursed is he who has intercourse with a woman in her anus.'
These are explicit prohibitions.
4
Analyze the Rational Proof (Qiyas)
The wife is called 'tilth' (harth) in verse 2:223, meaning she is for offspring like earth for cultivation. The anus is the place of feces (farth), not the place of cultivation, so it is unsuitable.
This is a qiyas jali.

باب الحيض
بينهما : إن كان في أوله : فدينار، وإن كان في آخره، أو وسطه: فنصف دينار.
- وهل ذلك على الرجل وحده، أو عليهما جميعاً؟
الظاهر أنه عليه، دونها.
- ومصرفه : مصرف الزكاة.
وله أن يُقبلها، ويضاجعها، ويستمتع بجميع بدنها ما خلا ما بين السرة والركبة عندهما، وقال محمد : يستمتع بجميع بدنها، ويجتنب شعار الدم، لا غير، وهو موضع خروجه.
ولا يحل لها أن تكتم الحيض على زوجها ؛ ليجامعها بغير علم منه. وكذا لا يحل لها أن تُظهر أنها حائض من غير حيض؛ لتمنعه مجامعتها؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لعن الله الغائصة والمغوصة»(۱). فالغائصة التي لا تُعلم زوجها أنها حائض، فيجامعها بغير علم.
